STAFT APPRAISAL REPORT
RUSSLAN FEDERATION
ENVMRONMENTAL MANAGEMENT PROJECT
ANNEX 3.1
POLICY AND REGULATORY SUPPORT
COMPONENT DESCRIPTION
A.    Background
1.     An overall framework of technical assistance priorities in environmental management was
developed jointly by the MEPNR, USG, the Canadian Government and the World Bank through a
series of missions from October 1992 to December 1993. A central element of this framework was
the need to strengthen the capacity to develop and implement environmental policies, in particular at
the federal and regional levels of government2L. It was agreed that particular attention should be given
to:
*      enhancing the capacity to set environmental priorities and to design policies to address
these priorities at federal and regional levels of government;
*      improving the system for monitoring environmental conditions and link the collection
of environmental data to the development and implementation of specific plans to
address the most serious environmental problems;
*      developing an effective legal and institutional framework for environmental
management including the capacity to formulate and enforce regulations, to coordinate
the activities of different agencies and levels of government, and to respond to public
concerns about environmental damage; and
*      ensuring that environmental policies and management practices take account of
external social, economic and technical changes by developing an integrated approach
to environmental quality and resource management and by working with economic
policymakers, enterprises and other institutions to ensure that environmental
considerations are properly taken into account in economic policies, as well as
investment and other decisions.
2.     This component has been designed to address these priorities. It emphasizes an integrated
approach to environmental management at regional and sectoral level by focusing on activities which
combine data collection, policy and regulatory development, implementation and enforcement. The
different skills -- technical, legal, economic and managerial -- that are required to ensure an effective
system of management are combined in the design of the component rather than being separated into
other components of the EMP and of the overall Framework Program.
3.     From a legal perspective, the new constitution specifies that the management of natural
resources, environmental protection and ecological safety, and nature protection are joint responsibil-
ities of the federal and the regional governments without providing detailed guidance to settle
21/ The terminology for describing sub-national levels of government in Russia is confusing, especially in translation. In the present context
dhe term 'regional' will be used to refer to subjects of federation (autonomous republics, oblasts and okrugs) as well as administrtive oblasts
and krais, or to groups of these units.



Annex 3.1                                                                             97
competing claims for jurisdiction on specific issues. The federal government is responsible for the
fundamental laws which govern natural resources and environmental protection. Thus, a workable
basis for environmental policy-making would give the responsibility for defining the overall priorities,
instruments and framework for environmental management to the federal authorities. Sub-national
authorities would be responsible for strategic planning at a regional level, as well as for the detailed
implementation and enforcement of policies and the allocation of financial resources.
4.     As a result, the central element of the Policy and Regulatory Support component will be the
elaboration and implementation of regional and sectoral environmental action plans for a small number
of highly polluted regions or of sectors responsible for disproportionate amounts of environmental
damage. The regions and sectors selected for this component overlap, so that measures to improve
the environmental performance of particular sectors will make a large contribution to reducing
environmental damage in the regions concerned. The process will strengthen regional capabilities to
formulate, implement and enforce environmental policies and regulations. For both practical and legal
reasons, long term progress towards the broad objective of reducing the environmental damage caused
to Russia's population and ecosystems will depend upon on an effective system of collaboration
between federal and regional levels of governmnent. The example of and lessons learnt during the
implementation of the subcomponent projects will provide a model that can be gradually extended
throughout the country. At the same time, the sectoral environmental action plans should benefit all
localities which are currently affected by the poor environmental performance of these sectors.
5.     A crucial characteristic of the EMP is that all of the components are designed to achieve
concrete changes in the policies, procedures or practices of environmental management which will
directly or indirectly lead to improvements in environmental conditions within a period of 3-4 years.
This is linked to the focus on federal-regional collaboration because the involvement of regional
authorities will be essential to turn policy and other initiatives into practical measures. While it is
difficult to set up criteria for judging the achievements of each of the activities in advance, the
successes and failures of the project and of this component must ultimately be judged by the extent
to which it has reduced the exposure of the population and of ecosystems to environmental damage.
B.    Objectives
6.     The principal objective of the policy and regulatory component is both simple and ambitious.
It is to achieve a significant reduction in environmental damage in the Urals and Upper Volga regions
within a period of 3-5 years with a particular focus on the impact of industrial pollution on human
health. The specific targets for reducing pollution cannot be set until the initial work of assessing the
scale of environmental damage and setting priorities has been carried out. However, they should
encompass reductions of up to 25 percent in ambient exposure to air pollutants such as lead,
particulates and toxic hydrocarbons, and to water pollutants such as heavy metals and toxic organic
compounds as well as bacteriological contamination of drinking water.
7.     The regions covered by the two regional activities will depend upon the willingness of the
regional authorities to cooperate with the project and to commit the required counterpart resources for
the implementation of the regional environmental action plans from their environment funds. The
regions of Chelyabinsk, Penn and Sverdlovsk will form the core of the Urals regional project with
the possible participation of the Bashkir Republic and the south-western part of Tyumen oblast. The
regions of Vologda and Yaroslavl will form the core of the Upper Volga regional project. The two
regions have been chosen to overlap with the regional activities being financed under the Hazardous
Waste and Water Quality Management components of the EMP, so as to promote an integrated
approach to environmental management. These regions are also the focus of the regional work to be



98                                                         Environmental Management Project
carried out under the Environmental Epidemiology component.  The process of assessing
environmental conditions and setting priorities will rely substantially on the work to be undertaken by
the Regional Environmental Epidemiology Units. Later, the monitoring of the impact of the
environmental measures adopted in the two regions will focus especially on tracking the health status
of sensitive groups of children and workers.
8.    The component has two subsidiary objectives
*     To develop the capacity to set environmental priorities, to formulate, implement and
enforce environmental policies, and to monitor environment conditions at federal, and
regional levels through a set of demonstration activities which can be gradually
extended to cover the whole country.
*     To establish the administrative, economic, legal and technical basis for reaching
negotiated agreements to reduce emissions from specific industries or in a particular
region over a period of years as the key element in a longer term approach to
reducing industrial pollution in Russia over the next 5-10 years.
9.     The achievement of these subsidiary objectives would provide a basis for ensuring continuing
improvements in environmental conditions both in the Urals and Upper Volga regions and in the rest
of the country by application of the approaches, policies and regulatory instruments developed in the
course of the project. Thus, the component would contribute to the ultimate objective of ensuring that
economic recovery and development in Russia is accompanied by reductions in environmental damage
rather than by worsening environmental conditions as in the past.
C.    Activities and Outputs
10.   The main focus of the activities to be undertaken in the Policy and Regulatory component will
gradually shift from the federal level to the regional level over the course of the project. The first
step will be the establishment of a Federal Environmental Policy Unit which will be responsible for
the initial training activities, for updating the National Environmental Action Plan, for developing the
legal and regulatory framework required to implement negotiated agreements for environmental
improvement, and for the first stage of the studies required to prepare Sectoral Environmental Action
Plans.
11.   Regional Environmental Policy Units will be established in the Urals and Upper Volga regions
-- based in Ekaterinburg and Yaroslavl respectively. The work program of these units will focus
initially upon preparing an assessment of regional environmental conditions and on establishing
environmental priorities on a regional and an obla&st basis. Then, with assistance from the sectoral
studies, they will draw up Regional Environmental Action Plans whose implementation will provide
the focus for the core work of the component.
12.   After the first year of the project the main attention of the Federal Unit will be on providing
support for the implementation and the extension of environmental policy initiatives under the Regional
Environmental Action Plans. Staff who have been working in the Federal Unit for an initial period
of training will return to work in the Regional Units, while legal, policy and sectoral specialists
employed by the Federal Unit will be seconded for periods to work in the Regional Units. To reduce
barriers between federal and regional policymakers and to ensure that experience in one region can
be shared with other regions all staff employed in the Federal Unit -- other than the Project Manager



Annex 3.1                                                                          99
and the team leaders -- will be required to spend at least 18 months seconded to one of the Regional
Units working on the implementation of local environmental action plans.
13.   Federal Environmental Policy Unit. This Unit will be established as an independent unit
reporting to and servicing the recently-established Commission on the Environment. This Commission
has been established by the Federal Council of Ministers to oversee the activities of a variety of
Ministries and State Committees whose responsibilities cover environmental and natural resource
management. Membership of the Commission includes the Ministry of Environrnental Protection and
Natural Resources, the Ministry of Agriculture, the State Forestry Service, and the State Committees
for Hydro-Meteorology, Sanitary-Epidemiological Surveillance, and Geology, as well as the Ministries
of Economy and Finance. The Commission is chaired by the Deputy Prime Minister responsible for
agricultural, environmental and natural resource issues. It represents the channel by which proposals
from individual Ministries and State Committees concerning environmental and natural resource issues
will be routed to the Council of Ministers for decision and execution. Since the original concept of
creating a single Ministry to cover all environmental and natural resource issues has been undermined
by the successful assertion of independence by various agencies, the Commission represents the best
framework for developing a coherent approach to environmental policymaking at the federal level.
14.   The activities of the Federal Unit will be divided between three teams: (a) a federal policy
team; (b) a regional policy team; and (c) a sectoral policy team. The federal policy teamn will be
responsible for:
*     the construction and maintenance of a database on ambient environmental conditions
and on major emission sources throughout the country;
*     the preparation of regular assessments of the extent of and trends in environmental
damage in different regions;
*     recommending priorities for federal environmental policies and activities which take
account of the damage to human health and to ecosystems caused by pollution, natural
resource use and other causes;
*     reviewing and updating the National Environmental Action Plan at regular intervals
in the light of changing environmental conditions and priorities;
*     developing the economic, legal and institutional framnework for the implementation of
federal environmental policies and regulations;
*     assisting in the development of the legal and institutional basis for environmental
impact assessment (EIA) and of a review mechanism to ensure that the quality and
effectiveness of EIA is maintained;
*     monitoring the implementation and effectiveness of federal environmental policies and
drawing up recommendations for changes designed to enhance their impact or to take
account of new information or changing circumstances;
*     working with non-environmental ministries and agencies to ensure that the environ-
mental consequences and costs of measures adopted by those bodies are taken fully
into account when decisions on economic policies, investments and other matters are
made;



100                                                         Environmental Management Project
*      developing a training strategy to enhance the knowledge and skills in environmental
management of staff working in federal, regional and local environmental bodies;
*      managing training courses in environmental law and environmental policy for staff
recruited to work in the Federal and Regional Units as well as workshops to
disseminate the results of experience gained during the project to regional and local
environmental officials throughout the country; and
*      providing technical assistance support to the NPAF for project feasibility studies and
project appraisals.
15.    The role of the regional team will be to coordinate and support the work being undertaken in
the Regional Environmental Policy Units to develop and implement policies to address local
environmental priorities. It will also be responsible for working with other regional governments to
develop environmental policy initiatives drawing upon the model provided by the project. The core
work of the team -- like that of the Regional Units -- will focus on achieving environmental
improvements in the two demonstration regions by a process of setting appropriate goals for
environmental policy and designing environmental measures which can implemented through a
combination of incentives, regulations, and investments involving negotiated agreements with industrial
enterprises and other bodies responsible for major emission sources in each of the two regions.
16.    The sectoral team will be responsible for drawing up and implementing Sectoral Environmental
Action Plans for 6 heavily polluting sectors with a primary focus on sources located in the
demonstration regions. The sectors to be covered by the team will be
*      iron and steel;
*     non-ferrous metals;
*     oil refining and petrochemicals;
-      basic organic and inorganic chemicals;
*      pulp and paper2-'; and
*      agriculture with a particular focus on intensive livestock operations.
17.   It is expected that work on the forestry sector will be financed from bilateral sources under
the auspices of other Bank sector work. The sectoral team will provide technical and other support
to the Regional Units to assist in the implementation of the Sectoral Environmental Action Plans within
the Urals and the Upper Volga regions. It will also assist other regional environmental authorities to
implement the Sectoral Plans by reaching negotiated agreements on emission reductions as well as
environmental quality and natural resource management issues with major enterprises and
organizations falling under their supervision. In addition this team will provide technical assistance
support to the National Pollution Abatement Facility for project feasibility studies and project
appraisals.
22/ The first phase of this sectoral study is being funded by the Finnish government.



Annex 3.1                                                                          10t
18.   The teams within the Federal Environmental Policy Unit define the functional responsibilities
of the unit, but as an organization it will operate according to matrix structure. Individual members
of staff will not assigned rigidly to one of the teams but will be expected to contribute to a variety of
tasks which may be managed by different teams. The combined skills of lawyers, economists and
policy specialists will be required for the work to be undertaken by all three teams, but the balance
between these skills will change over time and according to circumstances. Thus, a rigid vertical
structure would be both inefficient and would inhibit the sharing of experience which will be a crucial
element in ensuring that the component serves as an effective demonstration project in environmental
management.
19.   The outputs of the Federal Environmental Policy Unit will include
*     a regular assessment of the extent and trends in environmental damage in different
parts of the country;
*     an updated National Environmental Action Plan which should contain (a) a clear set
of environmental priorities with targets for environmental improvements to be
achieved within a 3-5 year period, and (b) recommendations for policies, regulatory
actions, institutional measures, and investments designed to meet these targets in a
cost-effective manner;
*     at least 6 Sectoral Environmental Action Plans which should focus on identifying a
set of low cost nieasures designed to reduce each sector's emissions of the key
pollutants up to 25 percent over 3-5 years together with programs for implementing
these measures in order to meet the emissions reduction targets;
*     recommendations and drafts of policies, legislation and regulations required to ensure
successful implementation of the National, Regional and Sector Environmental Action
Plans;
*     policy assessments, position papers and recommendations concerning the impact of
general economic and fiscal policies on pollution, natural resource use and other
environmental concerns; and
*     interim reviews and a final evaluation of the achievements of the component together
with recommendations for mechanisms to apply the lessons learned in the course of
the EMP to environmental management at the federal level and in regions throughout
the country.
20.   These outputs will be important indicators of the work being undertaken by the Federal
Environmental Policy Unit. Nonetheless, they will only be inputs to meeting the main goal of the
component which is to ensure that there is a significant improvement in the environmental quality
enjoyed by the Russian population over the length of the project.
21.   Regional Environmental Policy Units. For each region an Inter-Regional Environmental
Council either has or will be established. These will advise and supervise the work of the Regional
Environmental Policy Units. Each unit will cooperate with the regional authorities with environmental
responsibilities -- including the regional branches of federal Ministries and State Committees, regional
administrations and the Environment Committees of regional parliaments.

22.   The primary task for the Regional Units will be to draft, obtain approval for and oversee the
implementation of Regional Environmental Action Plans for each of the regiol Ls in the demonstration
regions. Carrying out this task will involve:
*     the collection and analysis of data on ambient environmental conditions and on major
emission sources;
*     the preparation of regular assessments of the extent of and trends in environmental
damage;
*     coordinating work on data collection and the assessment of environmen:al conditions
with the Regional Envi:onmental Epidemiology Units;
*     recommending priorities for regional environmental policies and activities which take
account of the damage to human health -- based, as far as possible, on the regional
epidemiological work -- and to ecosystems caused by pollution, natural resource use
and other causes;
*     preparation of the Regional Environmental Action Plans and updating them at regular
intervals in the light of changing environmental conditions and priorities;
*     providing support for the detailed implementation of federal environmental policies
and regulations at regional level;
*     advising on the level, assessment and collection of emission charges and on the
allocation of resources from regional and local environment funds
*     reviewing and recommending changes to "temporary" emission permits for enterprises
which operate in localities where ambient concentrations of pollutants exceed the
target levels set in the Regional Environmental Action Plans;
*     negotiating agreements with major emission sources to achieve phased reductions in
emissions over the period of the project;

*     providing policy and regulatory support to the regional activities of the Water Quality
and Hazardous Waste components of the EMP;
*     monitoring the effectiveness of environmental measures and drawing up recommenda-
tions for changes designed to enhance their impact or to take account of new
information or changing circumstances;
*     working with regional administrations, industrial enterprises, and NGOs to ensure that
the enviromnental consequences and costs of measures adopted by those bodies are
taken fully into account when decisions on economic policies, investments and other
matters are made.



Annex 3.1                                                                          103
23.   In essence, the work of the Regional Units will proceed in four phases.
*     During the first 6 months of their full operation they will focus on a rapid assessment
of environmental conditions in their regions and will draw up a preliminary set of
environmental priorities and targets for environmental improvement.
*     In months 7-12 these priorities and targets will be reviewed and agreed by all of the
interested parties with the results of these discussions being embodied in the Regional
Environmental Action Plans.
*     In months 13-24 the initial actions identified in the Regional Environmental Action
Plans will be implemented while the Regional Units will concentrate on the process
of negotiating agreements on emission reductions with major polluters. This will
involve the adoption of a carrot and stick approach with the carrot being assistance
from regional and local c-ivironment ftnds and the stick being the revocation of
"temporary" emission permits and the imposition of economic or regulatory sanctions
for breaches of the stricter standard emission norms.
*     In months 25-48 the full implementation of the Regional Environmental Action Plans
and of the negotiated emission reduction agreements will proceed and will be
monitored for their impact on environmental conditions. As appropriate, Regional
Environmental Action Plans will be updated in the final year of the project while the
sectors and enterprises covered by negotiated agreements will be extended to include
a larger number of medium-sized emission sources, as well as pollutants which were
not covered by the first round of agreements.
24.   Some staggering of this timetable for individual oblasts within each region will be required
in order to avoid putting undue demands on the resources of the Regional Units. The phasing will
be determined in the light of the initial assessment of regional environmental conditions and priorities.
Taking account of the overlapping timetables for the individual regions and regions, the main demand
for support from the regional and sectoral teams in the Federal Environmental Policy Unit will be
from months 12 to 36 as the Regional Units implement phases (ii), (iii) and the early part of phase
(iv) in the regions for which they are responsible.
25.   The outputs of the Regional Environmental Policy Units will include
*     regular assessments of the extent and trends in environmental damage in the two
regions;
*     Regional Environmental Action Plans which should contain (a) a clear set of
environmental priorities with targets for environmental improvements to be achieved
within a 3-5 year period, and (b) recommendations for policies, regulatory actions,
institutional measures, and investments designed to meet these targets in a cost-
effective manner;
*     negotiated agreements with major pollution sources to reduce emissions by up to 25
percent in a phased manner over a period of 3-5 years in order to meet the
environmental quality targets defined in the Regional Environmental Action Plans;



104                                                              Environmental Management Project
*      recommendations and drafts of policies, regulations and permit revisions required to
ensure successful implementation of the Regional and Sector Environmental Action
Plans;
*      interim  reviews and a final evaluation of the progress made in meeting the
environmental goals of the regional activities together with recommendations for
sustaining and extending environmental gains.
26.    As in the case of the Federal Environmental Policy Unit, these outputs are to be regarded as
intermediate steps in the process of enhancing environmental quality in the Urals and Upper Volga
regions.
D.     Implementation Arrangements
27.    The assistance will be provided over a period of 4 years starting in November 1994. The first
4 months of the project will be primarily devoted to providing specialized training courses in
environmental law and environmental policy for the prospective staff of the Federal and Regional
Units as well as on establishing offices and procuring equipment. Thus, the Federal and Regional
Units are expected to start full operation in April 1995.
28.    A  Policy and Regulatory Management Committee will be established by the Federal
Commission  on the Environment to supervise the implementation of the component.   This
Management Committee will include representatives from  the Ministries and State Committees
represented on the Commission, as well as representatives from other economic Ministries such as the
Ministries of Fuel and Energy and of Industry which will either be affected by or should work with
the Federal and Regional Units. Subject to the agreement of the Bank, the Management Committee
will appoint a Project Manager for the Policy and Regulatory Component who will also serve as the
Director of the Federal Environmental Policy Unit.
29.    The Federal and Regional Units will be staffed by Russian experts. The Federal Unit will
have a Director (the Project Manager), a Deputy Director who will be a qualified environmental
lawyerL' and will also act as the Unit's Chief Legal Adviser, and three team leaders for the federal,
regional and sectoral teams. At least 5 of the staff of the Federal Unit will be qualified environmental
lawyers, and a further 5 will have postgraduate qualifications in economics plus training in
environmental economics. The other five members of the unit will have technical qualifications with
a mix of multidisciplinary backgrounds. It will be condition of employment in the professional grades
of the Federal and Regional Units, except for the Director, that individuals must pass either a intensive
2-3 month training course in environmental law or one in environmental policy analysis before they
join the staff.
30.    The Urals Regional Unit will have a Director (at the same level as the team leaders in the
Federal Unit), at least 5 qualified environmental lawyers and 3 staff with postgraduate qualifications
in economics plus training in environmental economics. The Upper Volga Regional Unit will have
a Director, at least 3 qualified environmental lawyers and 2 staff with postgraduate qualifications in
economics plus training in environmental economics. Each of the Regional units will have 2 - 3
highly qualified technical experts.
23/ This context a qualified environmental lawyer is someone with a recognized law degree involving at least [121 semesters of higher education
plus a satisfactory performance in a full-time one semester course on environmental law such as that provided in the training program for
prospective staff.



Annex 3. 1                                                                           105
31.   The Directors and staff of the Federal and Regional Units will be selected according to
competitive procedures that will be established by the CPPI in consultation with the World Bank. The
Policy and Regulatory Management Committee will set up a selection committee for this purpose for
the Federal Units, while the Inter-Regional Environmental Councils will do the same for the Regional
Units for which they are responsible.
32.    A Policy and Regulatory Consultant will be appointed to provide policy advice and to
undertake specific studies during the course of the project. The terms of reference for this contract
will specify an initial set of studies and policy advice as well as an overall level of effort and set of
skills for the remainder of the work to be undertaken. In selecting the consultant a strong preference
will be given to proposals which are based on a team drawing on experience with environmental
policymaking and implementation in several countries with differing legal systems and approaches to
economic incentives and environmental regulations.
33.    The Policy and Regulatory Consultant will nominate and supervise the work of a small group
of independent, high level consultants (the Advisory Group). This Advisory Group will be responsible
for (a) advising the Project Manager on technical aspects of the implementation of the project, (b)
providing policy advice on critical issues, and (c) reviewing the overall progress of the component.
The Advisory Group will contain at least two Legal Advisers and at least two Economic Advisers with
a total membership of 5. It will meet with the Directors and senior staff of the Federal and Regional
Units at regular intervals (3-4 times per year) in order to maintain close contact with the work of these
units. They will also be expected to produce occasional papers or to provide on-the-spot policy advice
on specific issues which arise.  Members of the Advisory Group will be expected to devote
approximately 3 months per year to this task. Continuity of involvement is an essential element of
the role of the Advisory Group, nominees for membership of the Advisory Group will be expected
to commit themselves for the full period of the project, subject, of course, to special or unforeseen
circumstances which may necessitate withdrawal.
34.    The Advisory Group will be required to submit an annual report to the Management
Committee which reviews the work carried out in the previous 12 months and makes
recommendations, as appropriate, for steps required to speed up or enhance the effectiveness of the
work of the Federal and Regional Units.  This report will be submitted as an annex to the
Management Committee's annual review of the progress of the component which will be prepared for
MEPNR and the Bank.
35.   In addition to the Advisory Group two full-time foreign Senior Advisers will be appointed by
the Policy and Regulatory Consultant to assist the Project Manager in implementing the component
at both federal and regional levels. Each will work on the project for a period of two years starting
in July 1995. One of the Senior Advisers will be an environmental lawyer and the other will be an
environmental economist. Both will be expected to have substantial experience in the development
and implementation of environmental policies. Russian language skills will not be a pre-condition of
appointment but non-Russian speakers will be required to undertake an intensive Russian language
course before taking up their posts. The Senior Advisers will be chosen by a selection board including
the Project Manager, Ehe CPPI Director, representatives of the Management Committee and of the
Advisory Group. Their final appointment will be subject to the agreement of the Bank. The short-list
for consideration by the selection panel will be drawn up from applications received in response to
public advertisements in appropriate international magazines/journals.
36.   Equipment will be provided for the Federal and Regional Units to provide adequate office,
communications and computing facilities -- including electronic mail to link the various units with each



106                                                      Environmental Management Project
other as well as with other units established under the project and with foreign consultants. The
Federal and Urals Regional Units will have networked servers to enable them to manage and analyze
the databases on emission sources and environmental conditions as well as to model the impact of
proposed emission reductions on ambient pollution levels in the most polluted areas. Resources have
also been provided for the acquisition and installation of monitoring equipment to back up and assess
the effectiveness of the negotiated agreements between the environmental authorities and major
emission sources.
37.   Training is a crucial element of the component. As noted above, two intensive training
courses lasting 2-3 months each will be arranged at the beginning of the project. These courses will
partly be taught by foreign experts and partly by Russian experts. The courses will be taught in
Russian (with simultaneous translation if necessary) and all of the course materials will be translated
into Russian. After the courses have each been taught once with foreign assistance in developing the
course content and in teaching, it is intended that they should be repeated every year or two years with
Russian teaching staff and financed from fees or other local resources.
38.   Much of the training will occur on the job through close and continuing collaboration between
foreign advisers and their local counterparts. To reinforce and extend the experience gained in this
manner, a program of 3-4 month secondments will be established to enable many of the staff of the
Federal and Regional Units to work on concrete environmental policy issues in environmental agencies
or policy institutes in various market economies. The secondments must be well planned with clear
programs of work and responsibilities for the individuals concerned. Each work program will be
approved by the Project Manager in consultation with the Senior Policy and Legal Advisers and the
Policy Consultants' Advisory Group.
39.   A Training Consultant will be appointed to design and organize the formal training courses
to be provided at the beginning of the project and the program of secondments. The consultant should
include a Russian training institution in its team which can be responsible for taking over and
providing the formal training courses after the first year. The program of secondments proposed by
the consultant should cover more than one country, so that preference will be given to consultants
which can put together consortia of policy institutes and other appropriate agencies in several
countries.
40.   Resources have also been provided to hold workshops within Russia to disseminate the results
of the project and to train staff working for regional and local authorities other than those covered by
the project in the approach and methods followed in order to develop and implement regional and local
environmental action plans.
41.   In addition to the Policy and Regulatory Consultant and the Training Consultant, there will
be 6 sector consultancy contracts, one for each of the sectors to be covered by the sectoral team.
Each of these consultants will be responsible for drawing up a Sectoral Environmental Action Plan
in cooperation with the sectoral team in the Federal Unit and with the relevant Regional Units. It will
then be expected to provide support and advice for the process of the implementing the Action Plan,
especially with respect to the development of technical and economic proposals to underpin the
negotiation of emission reduction agreements with major polluters in the sector. Some of these
contracts may be funded by bilateral donors such as the preparation of an environmental action plan
for the pulp and paper sector which is being funded by the Finnish Government.
42.   It is envisaged that approximately half the funds provided for each contract will be allocated
to the development of the Sector Environmental Action Plan and the other half will be linked to the



Annex 3. 1                                                                           107
implementation of the Action Plan. Because this will involve the provision of advice and other
support over an extended period, preference will be given to consultants which propose joint teams
of foreign and Russian experts with a gradual transfer of skills, experience and responsibilities to the
Russian experts over the course of the project.



STAFF APPRAISAL REPORT
RUSSIAN FEDERATION
ENVIRONMENTAL MANAGEMIENT PROJEC
ANNEX 3.2
ENVIRONMENTAL EPIDEMIOLOGY COMPONENT
COMPONENT DESCRIPTION
A.    Background
1.    One of the most important reasons for concern about environmental degradation is its adverse
effect on human health. Information on the magnitude of environmental hazards and their impact on
human health is therefore very important for setting policy priorities. Environmental epidemiology
is concerned with the quantification of the human exposure to pollutants and its effects on public
health. Knowledge of the distribution of environmental hazards -- with respect to geographic region,
environmental medium, source, pollutant, and the link to specific health outcomes such as infant
mortality, cancer and birth defects -- is crucial for making informed policy decisions.
2.    Environmental epidemiology has been practiced in Russia for over forty years and specialists
in the field of environmental epidemiology are located in a number of cities throughout the country.
But despite a long research tradition, environmental epidemiology research in Russia is ill-organized
and of variable quality. Consistent information is not available for a range of pollutants and health
problems across all regions. A number of studies have been conducted on a regional level, but there
has been no effort to date to coordinate or evaluate the information from a national perspective. Thus,
policymakers are faced with the very difficult task of setting national and local priorities based on the
limited information currently available.
3.    There are serious institutional problems as well.  Investigations regarding the impact of
environmental pollution on human health in Russia have been carried out by a wide variety of agencies
in Moscow and around the country. There has been no coordinated strategy for the identification,
evaluation and control of threats to human health from environmental pollution. The Soviet health
care system was organized in a highly centralized and vertical manner and information tended to travel
only in an upward direction. As a result, local health officials and epidemiologists often had limited
access to national data. Correspondingly there is no tradition of local feedback on locally collected
information. A weak horizontal exchange of information meant that specialists who discovered a local
concentration of health anomalies may have been unaware of a similar occurrence in an adjacent
region.
4.    There also have been problems with the flow of environmental exposure information.
Responsibility for carrying out government-supported programs has been divided among numerous
agencies and jurisdictions. For example, there have been gaps and overlaps in the routine collection
of environmental monitoring data due to unclear division of labor between various health and
environmental institutions.   The dissemination of research on environmental epidemiology is
problematic in Russia.  Publications are few in number and lack detailed information.  Standard
publication of technical reports containing in-depth descriptions of methods has never been practiced.
As a consequence, changes in the coordination of regional efforts, the centralization and



Annex 3.2                                                                              109
systematization of data collection efforts, and improved dissemination of research findings will be
necessary to improve the system in which environmental epidemiology is currently practiced.
5.     Limitations on the availability and quality of environmental health data has had a serious
impact on the formulation and implementation of environmental policy. Russia has strict ambient
standards and there are sanitary zones around plants that generate significant levels of pollution which
should not be used for housing or similar purposes. These standards and regulations are violated in
most instances and the costs of bringing most plants into compliance will be very large. Thus, it is
essential to focus the limited resources available upon those emission sources which have the biggest
impact on human health. The practice of singling out the most sensitive groups of the population, like
infants and children, or most exposed groups of the population, like workers, for policy oriented
analysis does not exist in Russia. Therefore, providing a consistent framework for collecting and
assessing environmental health information on infants and workers is a fundamental element in the
development of a cost-effective approach to environmental regulation.
6.     Data reported by Soviet officials indicate that the cost of environmental degradation in terms
of human health has been high. For example, in 1989, the USSR State Committee for Environmental
Protection referred to a study, conducted by the Institute of Hygiene and Preventive Medicine for
Children and Adolescents, which claimed that the prevalence of nervous disorders, allergies and
gastrointestinal illness among children had doubled between the 1960s and the 1980s, though it is not
clear to what extent environmental factors played a role in this increase. Mortality data suggest that
the health of the Russian population was improving through the 1970s, but has stagnated because of
the economic downturn and continuing low investments in health care.   Both adult and infant
mortality levels in the Russian Federation are considered high by western standards, and it is likely
that environmental hazards are a contributing factor. These estimates are highly unreliable because
of poor control of data generation.
7.     Concern about these hazards has prompted the development of computerized information
systems which will be used for environmental epidemiology by local and regional authorities in
various parts of the country. For instance, Tyumen invested DM4 million for such a system while
Bakov, Cherepovetz, Elekstrostal and the Komi republic have started similar initiatives. Such
activities take place independently with little coordination or quality control. To prevent idiosyncratic
developments where information cannot be pooled or matched, methodological and technical
standardization is needed.  (e.g. cross-calibrations of monitoring devices, use of standard
questionnaires, sample selection methods, protocols etc.).
8.    It is widely accepted that the quality of environmental and health data in Russia is extremely
uneven, so that the inherent variance of the data swamps differentials associated with systematic
environmental health hazards.
B.    Objectives
9.     The environmental health component of EMP has three basic objectives:
(i)    To develop federal and regional capacity to generate, collect, organize and interpret
environmental health data so as to provide a systematic basis for assessing
environmental health risks and setting environmental priorities at regional and federal
levels.



110                                                        Environmental Management Project
(ii)   to improve information about the relationship between environment and health in
Russia with an emphasis on monitoring the impact of changing environmental
conditions on the health of populations at the regional level.
(iii)   To carry out baseline and follow-up surveys, or site specific studies of a more
exploratory kind to establish the extent to which pollution is affecting the health of
children and workers, including populations living in sanitary zones.
10.   There is a significant degree of overlap between these objectives, so that federal and regional
initiatives will contribute towards meeting both objectives. However, it is important to distinguish
between them because they address problems faced by different branches of government. The first
focuses specifically on the policy concerns of the environmental authorities at federal and regional
level, since they are responsible for setting priorities, drafting and implementing environmental
legislation and allocating government resources available for environmental improvements.  The
second focuses on the broader concerns of those dealing with public health issues -- as well, of course,
as the fears of the public at large -- about the contribution of environmental factors to differentials in
mortality and morbidity rates across regions and countries.   The final objective links the
environmental health to environmental quality components and provides a systematic framework for
assessing the impact of policy-induced and other changes in exposure to pollution on the health of the
most vulnerable and/or most exposed groups of the population.
C.    Assistance Strategy
ll.    The contract for the component is expected to be awarded to one general contractor,
representing a consortium of research institutes and academia from at least two continents.
Preference in selecting the Consultant will be given to those whose teams mobilize staff and experience
from environmental and health institutes in more than one country and more than one continent. The
assistance will extend over a period of 4 years starting in November 1994. Approximately two-thirds
of the Consultant's inputs are expected to be provided in the second and third year of the contract.
12.   The Consultant should liaise closely with other consultant teams undertaking work for other
components of the Environmental Management Project. Training is a crucial element. Much of it
will take place through close and continuing collaboration between foreign advisors and their local
counterparts.  A part of the formal training program  is designed to precede any subsequent
implementation of the project.
13.   The sub-component projects involve the secondment of staff, for variable periods, to gain
practical experience by working at an Institute or other organization operated by the Consultant or its
subcontractors. These secondments will include some formal coursework, but their primary objective
is to train staff and to carry out environmental epidemiology investigations by working along with
others on similar studies. The secondments will be well planned with clear programs of work and
responsibilities for the individuals concerned.  Each work program -- in particular, the study or
studies to which the individual will be contributing -- will be approved by the Subcomponent Project
Manager in consultation with the Management Committee for that subcomponent.
14.   The lack of communication and exchange of information is a major constraint in the present
state of Russian environmental epidemiology. Therefore, strengthening of existing journals including
the existing newsletter of the MEPNR, and support for publication fees of foreign journals is provided
for under the Project.



Annex 3.2                                                                        111
D.    Counterparts and Implementation Arrangements
15.   The responsible department in MEPNR for this component is the Department of Ecological
Safety. A Component Management Committee consisting of representatives of MEPNR, the State
Committee for Sanitary and Epidemiological Surveillance (GOSKOMSANEPIDNADZOR), the State
Committee for Hydrometereology (ROSGIDROMET), the Ministry of Health, the Ministry of
Economic Affairs, the Russian Academy of Sciences, and the Russian Academy of Medical Sciences
has been set up to advise and supervise the work of the Subcomponent Project Managers at federal
and regional levels. The Federal Program Manager will be responsible for the management of the
federal level subcomponent, and the coordination of the two regional initiatives. He will be
responsible for the federal subcomponent technical subject areas such as the annual federal report,
federal databases and policy oriented analyses. He will be an ex-officio member of the subcomponent
Management Committee and will be assisted in his work by the General Consultant Firm, as outlined
in this firm's Terms of Reference.
16.   The federal Subcomponent Project Manager will lead a team of Russian experts who have been
seconded for the project. The Foreign Consultant Firm will provide foreign advisors to work with
this team, as well as the two regional implementation teams in the Urals and Upper Volga under
regional Subcomponent Project Managers. The two regional Subcomponent Project Managers will
report to Regional Subcomponent Management Committees under the Upper Volga and Urals Inter-
regional Environmental Councils, respectively.
E.    Activities and Outputs
17.   The environmental epidemiology component will focus on the following activities, which will
be incorporated into one federal subcomponent and two regional subcomponent projects:
3     Establish a Federal Environmental Epidemiology Center and strengthen federal
facilities and institutes in Moscow with particular emphasis on developing the capacity
to provide assessments of environmental health priorities relevant for national
legislation and policy.
*     Establish two Environmental Epidemiology Centers in the Urals and Upper Volga
regions to provide the essential expertise for the collection and analysis of data, and
support for environmental and health officials in regional governments. Undertake
specific investigations of the impact that emissions from individual plants have on the
health of the population at risk.
*     Develop the capability to enable regional authorities in the Urals region and the region
of the Upper Volga to develop their own policy priorities based on regional
assessments of environmental health conditions.
*     Improve the existing system for generating, collecting, managing and analyzing data
on infant and child health as the basis for monitoring the consequences of changes in
population exposure to  various pollutants. Data on variables such as the birth
weight, birth defects, infant diseases and child development can be sensitive indicators
for the impact of environmental conditions on the population in general.
*     Improve the existing Russian system to design and manage a program to collect and
analyze data on the health status and environmental conditions of working in different



112                                                      Environmental Management Project
industrial sectors of the economy and populations in industrial sanitary zones who are
at greatest risk due to environmental health impacts.
*     Develop and provide a series of policy oriented training courses in environmental
epidemiology.
*     Develop twinning relationships with foreign policy oriented environmental health
institutes.
SUB-COMPONENT 1:           THE ESTABLISHMENT OF A FEDERAL
ENVIRONMENTAL EPIDEMIOLOGY CENTER
18.   The Federal Environmental Epidemiology Center will be responsible for providing support
and coordination for regional and federal initiatives on environmental epidemiology. Its efforts will
initially be focused on six principal areas:
*     Preparation of an annual report on environmental health in the Federation. This
annual report will be divided into two sections. The first section will provide an
overview of the incidence of health problems linked to environmental factors with
tables and maps showing the distribution of environmental hazards based on exposure
to pollutants in air, water and soil. It will also review evidence relating to the impact
of changing environmental conditions on the state of human health in Russia. The
framework of preparing such a general overview should provide the basis for
developing and disseminating a set of national priorities with respect to the incidence
and causes of environmental health problems. In the initial stage of the project this
report will be a critical evaluation of existing reports. The second section will
provide a detailed survey of relevant and well-founded studies on a particular issue
in environmental health -- such as the problems caused by exposure to lead and other
heavy metal dusts, or the contribution of environmental factors to differentials in the
incidence of respiratory diseases. This will summarize the findings of more than 100
institutes around the country and offer reference material on good practice in
environmental epidemiology for those undertaking specific local studies of particular
environmental health problems. The annual report will make an objective evaluation
of reported results and findings, and will highlight deficiencies in methodologies and
approaches.
*     Assessment and improvement of the quality of enviromnental health data. The
federal center would examine factors pertaining to the quality of existing data such as
methods of sample selection, chronological and geographical coverage, validity and
completeness, process of data generation, feedback between generation and analysis
of data, etc. The primary focus of the work is to identify good quality data that can
be used for assessing environmental health priorities and to develop methods of
improving 'poor quality' data for inclusion in this assessment. For instance, the
presently reported oscillation of national mortality rates during the last few years is
unrealistic. The development of a framework for generating, collecting and analyzing
standardized mortality data by districts (rayons) rather than just by Oblast is desirable.
In this way small area variations in mortality rates can be identified and linked to
differential exposure to various pollutants.    This is already being done in
Ekaterinburg (see below) and a small number of other Oblasts, but the system needs
to be extended on a consistent basis to cover a much larger sample of Oblasts. At



Annex 3.2                                                                            113
a minimum, the compilation of this database might initially focus on the Oblasts
covered by the two Regional Environmental Epidemiology Units in cooperation with
the central support group, but plans should be made for a gradual extension of its
coverage to include all Oblasts and autonomous republics which wish to be involved.
Some software and analytical tools have already been developed, so that the issue is
to ensure that variables and classifications are defined in a consistent manner and that
the necessary information from death certificates is recorded on a regular basis.
Another example is support for developing morbidity surveillance programs based on
population samples in urban areas. Such programs contain data on disease incidence
by broad diagnostic category and cover most of the urban centers in Russia where
there are significant environmental health concerns. Along with the local mortality
database (provided the data quality is acceptable), they should serve as the first line
of inquiry for those wishing to investigate environmental influences on human health.
*     Vulnerable Groups in the Population: Children and Infants. The project will
provide technical support at the federal and regional level for: (a) the generation,
collection and analysis of standardized data on infant and child health focusing on the
impact of environmental conditions on such variables as birth weights and defects,
infant mortality, and respiratory and gastro-intestinal illnesses, and (b) the
development of procedures and programs to monitor the consequences of changes in
environmental conditions on various indicators of child growth. Data on infant and
child health are a useful basis for monitoring changes in the impact of environmental
conditions on human health. There are a number of regional and federal initiatives
on this issue being proposed or undertaken by institutes associated with the Ministry
of Health and Sanepidnadzor. The purpose will be to coordinate and focus these
efforts. Thus the most useful information and results can be obtained for guiding the
development of environmental policies in the light of feedback from evidence on
infant and child health.  As a national program  it will also provide training and
support for those working in this field. Existing procedures for registering data on
infant and child health are, in any case, already being revised and improved. What
is needed, however, is to combine these data with information on local environmental
conditions. By monitoring subsequent changes in the incidence of the infant/child
health problems, which are most sensitive to environmental conditions, it will be
possible to create direct indicators for measuring changes in environmental health.
*     Most exposed sectoral groups in industrial plants and their vicinity (including
sanitary zones). There is a considerable uncertainty about the relative contributions
of occupational and general population exposures to various health problems
associated with industrial pollutants such as benzo-pyrenes, chlorinated hydrocarbons
and heavy metals (to name a few). This task will collect data and undertake analyses
designed to distinguish between occupational and general environmental factors in
order to assist the authorities to establish an appropriate balance between measures
designed to limit occupational exposures within plants and those intended to improve
environmental conditions outside plant boundaries. This will, in turn, contribute to
the formulation of policies with respect to the sanitary zones around large industrial
plants, which often include housing for the families of those working at the plants as
well as others. Recommendations based on these efforts will also contribute to the
design of regulatory system(s) to be developed by other components of the EMP.



1 14                                                       Environmental Management Project
*     Coordination of the Regional Environmental Epidemiology Centers - in terms of
training, secondment of foreign consultants, methodology, concentration on special
targeted groups in the population and quality assurance.  The federal unit's
coordination activities should concentrate particularly on the methodology of the
assessment of environmental health hazards, the collection and maintenance of
standardized databases of regional mortality and morbidity data related to
environmental conditions, and the improvement of the quality of environmental health
data. The federal center will second technical staff and will arrange for foreign
experts to work in the two regional epidemiological units.
*     The development of a training program for staff working in Federal and Regional
Environmental Epidemiology Centers, research institutes, and regional government
units concerned with environmental health. The foreign consultant's responsibility
will be to train trainers' and to assist in the development of case studies, course
materials and on developing an overall training strategy. The formal training would
be such that the program, at least partly, would be taught by local staff after the first
year of the project. The program will provide training in all aspects of environmental
epidemiology and the management of environmental health data for staff concerned
with environmental health issues in all parts of the country. The initial formal
training program will take eight weeks and includes specially organized courses or
training workshops for the staff involved in the project. The program will begin with
a course on practical evaluation of regional environmental health problems. The
initial program will consist of an initial course, supplemented by more advanced
courses on environmental epidemiology focused on the practical relevance of
environmental epidemiology for environmental policies. The course program would
address basic issues related to descriptive and analytical environmental epidemiology,
including:  routine monitoring of health and environment and it's role in
environmental epidemiology; basic designs of epidemiological surveys; methods of
collection of data on health and on exposure to environmental factors in
epidemiological surveys; control of confounding; principles of statistical analysis of
survey data; study results reporting, risk communication, policy implications of
environmental epidemiology studies; microcomputer use for epidemiologists; and basic
elements of quality assurance/quality control of laboratory procedures in application
to environmental health issues. Workshops on comparative experience and seminars
to present the results of work that has been undertaken will be held to ensure
cooperation and consistency between the Environmental Epidemiology Centers in
different parts of the country.
*     The courses would define follow-up activities to be conducted by the participants
within a defined time after the course. The activities would be a part of the overall
program to be undertaken under the project. To assure the effectiveness of the formal
training program, the number of participants in each session would not exceed twenty-
five. The program will be repeated throughout the course of the project with
increased involvement of local staff in teaching. After two years the local staff would
be able to teach the complete program  independently of the foreign expert's
assistance. The program would devote a substantial part of the training to issues on
child health and on occupational health related issues. These issues should be built
into the formal courses on environmental epidemiology as mentioned above.

19.   The Foreign Consultant will establish and operate a twinning arrangement between the Federal
Center and one or more foreign institutes with substantial experience in the application of
environmental epidemiology to the development of federal and regional environmental policies. The
arrangements would not involve a rigid framework in which one partner institute is paired with one
or more regional centers, since a matrix framework may be more satisfactory for providing technical
support in different areas of expertise.  The Consultant would encourage cooperation between the
regional centers as well as with their partner institutes.   The Federal Center will have the

for periods of 6 months each, to gain experience in working on issues and studies

review and replication studies whose findings are essential for the annual report will

mortality data, (c) the generation, collection and analysis of morbidity data, and (d)
the preparation of guidelines on data generation, collection, management and study
protocols to improve the quality and comparability of environmental health data and
studies in different parts of the country; and
e     Technical support for the regions for (a) the generation, collection and analysis of
standardized mortality data, (b) the generation, collection and analysis of morbidity
data under existing programs, (c) the provision of specialist advice and training in
environmental epidemiology for regional research institutes, Sanepidnadzor stations
in the region, regional environment and health departments, and others concerned with
environmental health problems in the region and (d) the development of regional
strategies to address environmental health problems.
SUB-COMPONENT 2:           ESTABLISHMENT OF TWO REGIONAL
ENVIRONMENTAL EPIDEMIOLOGY INITIATIVES.
20.   It is proposed that regional environmental epidemiology initiatives would be established as a
demonstration for regional system for generating, collecting, managing and analyzing data on regional
environmental health conditions. The regions that have been selected for this initial program are: the
Upper-Volga and the Urals.
21.   The objective of the regional initiatives will be to strengthen regional capacity, and to identify
and monitor environmental health priorities in collaboration with Oblast and municipal authorities in
charge of environmental and health policies. Their tasks will include:
*     Overseeing the generation, collection and management of environmental health data
and, as appropriate, acting to ensure the quality and consistency of such data;
*     Providing epidemiological expertise and specialist advice to improve the quality of
analyses of environmental health by local research institutes and other bodies;
*     Concentrate on infant and child health and occupational health;



116                                                         Environmental Management Project
*      Assisting Oblast, municipal and district environmental authorities in determining their
environmental health priorities as a basis for formulating regional environmental
priorities to guide the allocation of regional environmental funds, the negotiation and
enforcement of emission standards and the development of regional environmental
initiatives; and
*      Collaboration with research institutes and industrial plants in the region to design and
carry out reliable studies on the impact of pollution from individual plants on the
health of regional populations.
A.     The Urals Regional Environmental Health Initiative.
22.    Environmental health concerns are urgent in the Urals region (specifically in the Oblasts within
the area from Perm and Ekaterinburg in the north to Chelyabinsk in the center and Magnitogorsk in
the south), because of the high concentration of heavily polluting industries. These industries are
likely to experience substantial restructuring within the next five years. At the same time, Oblast and
municipal authorities will be playing an increasingly important role in monitoring and regulating
environmental conditions under their jurisdiction. These authorities will require substantial assistance
from a Regional Environmental Epidemiology initiative to support the development of their
environmental priorities and to monitor the impact of policies to mitigate environmental health damage
associated with past production, as well as current emissions.
23.    The purpose of the Urals Initiative is to build upon existing efforts in order to provide a
demonstration of the ways in which environmental epidemiology can contribute to the formulation of
environmental policies by assessing environmental health priorities and the potential impact of
alternative measures to address them. The local Sanepidnadzor station in Ekaterinburg stands out for
the general quality of its equipment, the expertise of its staff and its commitment to tackling regional
environmental health concerns.  There exists also a close cooperation between this station and the
Oblast Environmental and Health authorities because of the specific involvement of the Deputy
Governor of the Oblast who chairs the relevant coordinating committees.  Ekaterinburg has seven
institutes active in the field of environmental epidemiology: the Institute of Hygiene (Sanepidnadzor);
the Oblast Center of Sanepidnadzor financed by the Oblast (FAV); the Medical Institute, the Medical
Genetic Center for the Oblast (OBLZDRAV) and The Mother and Child Health Institute, all belonging
to the Ministry of Health; the Institute of Industrial Ecology of the Urals branch of the Russian
Academy of Sciences; and the Paediatric Hospital of the Oblast administration. These circumstances
provide an excellent framework for establishing a Regional Environmental Epidemiology initiative that
will lead the way in establishing the necessary collaborative links between regional environmental
policymakers and those working on environmental health problems.
24.    The Urals Initiative will encompass the two main Oblasts in the Urals region. The initiative
will provide support for studies of environmental conditions and for formulating priorities in each of
the Oblasts according to the tasks described in Sub-component 1 above.



Annex 3.2                                                                          117
25.   The Foreign Consultant will, through the federal unit, establish and operate a twinning
arrangement between the technical staff in the Urals Region and one or more overseas Institutes with
substantial experience in the application of environmental epidemiology to the development of regional
environmental priorities and initiatives in areas with a large concentration of heavy industry. This
twinning arrangement should cover, inter alia:
*     The secondment of 4-5 members of the regional staff to partner institutes for periods
of 6 months each, to gain experience in working on issues and studies relevant to the

*     Technical support for: (a) the generation, collection and analysis of standardized

of populations living close to large industrial plants; (d) the provision of specialist

B.    The Upper Volga Regional Environmental Health Initiative.
26.   Environmental health concerns are an urgent priority in the region of the Upper Volga,
specifically in the Yaroslavl and Vologda Oblasts. Location of major polluting industries in these
Oblasts discharging into the Upper Volga River affects the whole river basin up to the Moscow area.
These industries are likely to experience substantial restructuring within the next five years. At the
same time, Oblast and municipal authorities will be playing an increasingly important role in
monitoring and regulating environmental conditions under their jurisdiction. These authorities will
require substantial assistance from a Regional Environmental Epidemiology initiative to support the
development of their environmental priorities and to monitor the impact of policies to mitigate
environmental health damage associated with past production as well as current emissions.
27.   The purpose of the Upper Volga Initiative is to build upon existing efforts of the regional
authorities and MEPNR within the framework of Ecological Disaster Zone (EDZ) designation of the
Cherepovitz area, regional activities for other components of the EMP and environmental effects olt
the whole river basin. Plans already exist to integrate the data of the air-monitoring system with the
health data of the Sanepidnadzor in Cherepovetz. The latter is well organized, well equipped with
computers and well connected with the Municipal Health Committee and Oblast Environmental
Committees of Yaroslav and Vologda Oblasts. These circumstances provide an excellent framework
for establishing a Regional Environmental Epidemiology Center in Cherepovetz that will also lead the
way in collaboration between regional environmental policymakers and those working on
environmental health problems.
28.   The Upper Volga Initiative will provide support for studies of environmental conditions and
for formulating priorities in each of the Oblasts according to the tasks described in Sub-component
A.  Due to deficiencies in the existing data, there is considerable uncertainty about the relative
contributions of occupational and general population exposures to various health problems associated
with industrial pollutants such as: carbon bisulphide; nitrogen dioxide; sulphur dioxide; and lead
(Cherepovetz); phenol and hydrogen sulphide (Yaroslavl); and hydrocarbons and hydrogen sulphide
(Tver). The Initiative will collect data and undertake analyses designed to distinguish occupational



118                                                         Environmental Management Project
and general environmental factors in order to assist the authorities to establish an appropriate balance
between measures designed to limit occupational exposures within plants and those intended to
improve environmental conditions outside plant boundaries.  This will, in turn, contribute to the
formulation of a policy with respect to the sanitary zones around large industrial plants which often
include housing for the families of those working at the plants, as well as others.
29.    The Foreign Consultant will, through the federal unit, establish and operate a twinning
arrangement between the technical staff that is seconded to the Upper Volga region and one or more
overseas Institutes with substantial experience in the application of environmental epidemiology to the
development of regional or local environmental priorities and initiatives in areas with a large
concentration of heavy industry. This twinning arrangement would cover, inter alia:
*      The secondment of 2-3 members of the regional staff to partner institutes for periods
of 6 months each, to gain experience in working on issues and studies relevant to the
environmental health problems in the Region of the Upper Volga; and
*      Technical support for: (a) the generation, collection and analysis of standardized
mortality data; (b) the generation, collection and analysis of morbidity data under
existing programs; (c) studies to examine the relative importance of occupational and
general environmental exposure to industrial pollutants in determining the health status
of populations living close to large industrial plants; (d) the provision of specialist
advice and training in environmental epidemiology for, Sanepidnadzor stations, local
environment and health departments, and others concerned with environmental health
problems in the region or the Oblast; and (e) the development of regional strategies
to address environmental health problems.
F.    Reporting
30.    The Consultant would submit a series of regular tri-yearly progress reports reviewing their
activities and assessing progress towards achieving the project objectives for each of the
sub-components. These should enumerate and briefly describe: (a) the inputs, activities and outputs
of the last period; (b) the contribution to the project objectives; (c) problems encountered, remedies
sought and further remedies proposed; (d) detailed plans for the coming periods and suggestions for
changes to the plans for later periods; and (e) any other issues. Reports on completed studies and
other material -- including working papers, training materials and descriptions of databases -- produced
in the course of the activities should be annexed to these regular reports.
31.    An inception report for the project should be submitted at the end of month 3, a midterm
report at the end of month 24 and a final report at the end of month 48. These reports should
encompass the regular quarterly reports due in the relevant months.
32.    Reports will be submitted to the Ministry of Environmental Protection and Natural Resources
as well as other agencies specified by the Government in a total of at least eight Russian language and
two English language copies. At least two English language copies should be submitted to the Bank.
