6.     During project preparatory visits to the Sverdlovsk Oblast, the Oblast government, local
agencies, and environmental organizations expressed a desire for project support under the Water
Management Component. Based on the major concerns and suggested subcomponent project activities,
the primary objectives are to: (1) assess the threat to public health from drinking water supplies and
sources of supply for Ekaterinburg; (2) evaluate current infrastructure needs and the institutional and
technical framework for supplying potable water and protecting its quality; (3) recommend physical,
operational, legal, financial, and institutional improvements; (4) demonstrate specific measures to
reduce threats to public health; and (5) strengthen local/Oblast institutions for drinking water
management.
C.    Scope of Work
7.     Following is the proposed scope of work for this subcomponent project.
Task 1        Public Health Risk Characterization
la.    Collect and evaluate available data on raw and drinking water quality and
potential health effects, identify data gaps, and collect additional data as
needed.
lb.    Conduct comparative health risk appraisal for direct risks from drinking water
and indirect risks from related exposures (e.g., swimming and fish
consumption).
Ic.    Conduct a system vulnerability assessment and identify the sources and/or
causes of greatest risk.
Id.    Recommend corrective actions and/or additional steps to further characterize
risks and corrective measures.
Task 2        Facilities and Operations Audit.
2a.    Develop procedures and process for a standard facilities and operations audit.



Annex 3.3.3                                                                              147
2b.    Summarize the components, capacities, demands, condition, operation, and
energy use of existing facilities, including sources, water and wastewater
treatment plants, and pumping, storage, distribution, and collection systems.
Include input from consultants and contractors and a description of their role.
2c.    Assess needs relative to water demands, wastewater loads, and acceptable
standards of design, construction, and operation.
2d.    Define major system needs/priorities for rehabilitating and upgrading existing
facilities. Recommend future implementation actions.
Task 3        Financial and Administrative Review
3a.    Review present financial situation including rate structure, revenues, and
costs.
3b.    Assess the ability of existing  institutional, legal, and administrative
arrangements in relation to the planning, financing,   operation, and
maintenance of facilities and services.
3c.    Evaluate alternatives for improving current arrangements.
3d.    Develop alternative capital budgets based on the financial assessment and the
needs identified in Task 2d, under different assumptions, revenues (water
rates), and sources of finance.
3e.    Prepare a report of findings, recommendations, priorities, and implementation
steps.
Task 4        Standards, Codes, and Guidance Manuals
4a.    Review current practices, procedures, and standards for water and wastewater
system design, operation, and maintenance, including sources, storage, and
distribution facilities, and appurtenances. Include input of support consultants
and contractors.
4b.    Identify limitations and  develop model standards, codes, and/or guidance
manuals for Ekaterinburg.
4c.    Conduct a training and demonstration program focusing on cross connection
elimination, including computerized (GIS) mapping and analysis of the
distribution system and elimination of cross connections in the demonstration
area.
4d.    Promote adoption and use of standards, codes, and cross connection
elimination measures.



148                                                         Environmental Management Project
Task S        Reservoir Operation and Rational Use Demonstration
5a.    Develop a demonstration project to evaluate and successfully illustrate more
efficient reservoir operations, water allocations, and the feasibility of reducing
industrial use of potable water for non-potable purposes (without adversely
impacting water revenues, industry profitability, or receiving water quality).
Sb.    Select reservoir(s) and industry(ies) meeting requirements for a successful
demonstration.
5c.   Implement demonstration project and document results.
5d.    Promote similar approaches for other reservoirs and industries.
Task 6        Information Program for Decision Makers and Water Customers
6a.    Develop an education program and materials to inform (1) decision makers
of major facility and administrative needs, and (2) water customers of the
value and cost of reliable potable water service. Relate product to price and
identify needed improvements.
6b.   Implement program and monitor impact.
Task 7        Specialist Training
7a.    Develop courses and materials for training specialist in laboratory analysis,
water and wastewater treatment plant operation, and maintenance of the
distribution and collection systems.
7b.    Provide instructor training to current employees or others that can provide
training on a routine basis.
7c.    Conduct initial courses, evaluate effectiveness, and revise programs and
materials as necessary.
Task 8        Water Supply System Monitoring and Data Management Demonstration
8a.    Review existing data on the quality of raw water sources and delivered
potable water. Report data gaps and priorities for additional sampling, and
improvements.
8b.    Review the monitoring objectives, responsibilities, laboratory capabilities, and
monitoring design process of the agencies involved in water resource
monitoring different components of the water supply system. Report on
potential duplication and opportunities for cooperation and increased
efficiencies in laboratories and monitoring programs.



Annex 3.3.3                                                                          149
8c.    Upgrade laboratory and data management capabilities of the Oblast
Environmental Committee for one or more of the critical water management
needs (e.g., candidate equipment includes atomic absorption, gas
chromatograph, glassware, sample containers).
8d.    Demonstrate improved monitoring approaches, laboratory analyses, and data
management using preliminary screening of reservoir and drinking water
"hotspots". Include sediment, fish tissue, toxicity, and priority pollutant
analysis.
8e.    Develop standard procedures and guidelines for the design and implementation
of monitoring programs, including data management and analysis.
Task 9       Watershed Management Demonstration
9a.    Evaluate  feasibility  of Volchikhinskoye  Reservoir  watershed  as  a
demonstration site and select alternative watershed if necessary.
9b.   Inventory pollution sources within the watershed and quantify waste loads.
9c.    Determine watershed protection needs and evaluate current pollution control
requirements and enforcement programs. Include feasibility of separating
major wastewater discharges from the water supply source (e.g.,transporting
discharge to another watershed).
9d.    Prepare a watershed protection plan recommending pollution control,
legislative, enforcement, and economic incentive actions for adequately
protecting water supply sources.
D.    Outputs
8.            (1)    Defined  direct and  indirect public  health  risks  and  prevention
recommendations.
(2)    A ten-year capitalization program for upgrading and rehabilitating water
supply and wastewater system facilities/operations.
(3)    Standard procedures for a facilities/operations audit.
(4)    Recommendations for financial and administrative improvements in water
system operations.
(5)    Recommendations  for  improved  legal,  financial,  and  institutional
arrangements for management of the water system.
(6)    Model procedures, codes, and standards for design, operation, and
maintenance of the water system.
(7)    Cross connection elimination program and demonstration.
(8)    Geographic Information System map of the distribution system and computer
capabilities to assist in analyzing and managing the system.
(9)   Improved skills in optimizing reservoir operations and water allocations
(10)   Demonstration of industrial water conservation to reduced potable water
demand.
(11)  Improved laboratory equipment and capabilities.



150                                                      Environmental Management Project
(12)  Improved specialist skills and training programs for treatment plant operators,
laboratory specialists, and distribution system maintenance personnel.
(13)   Recommendations for coordinating monitoring and laboratory efforts to
reduce costs, avoid duplication, and increase data value.
(14)   New data and procedures for defining contamination "hot spots" within the
distribution system and water sources.
(15)   Guidelines  for designing  and  implementing  monitoring  programs
Demonstration of watershed pollution inventory techniques and management
planning to protect water resources.
(16)  Increased communication, cooperation, and data exchange among the key
water management agencies.



SrAFF APPRAISAL REPORT
RUSSIAN FEDERATION
ENVIRONMENTAL MANAGEMENT PROJECT
ANNEX 3.4.1
DEVELOPMENT OF A NATIONAL INDUSTRIAL WASTE
DATA MANAGEMENT SYSTEM
SUBCOMPONENT DESCRIPTION
A.    Background
1.           This subcomponent project is one of two core subcomponents to be executed by the
Russian Federation as part of the Environmental Management Project (EMP), Hazardous Waste
Component. The purpose of the Hazardous Waste Component is to provide key elements of technical
assistance to the Russian Federation at the national and regional level in their efforts to:
3     prevent the further build-up of hazardous wastes which pose a health threat to
workers, the population at large, and threaten the economic viability of enterprises
over the longer term;
3     develop programs for prevention of formation (where possible) and\or recycle or re-
use of hazardous wastes;
3     improve the management of hazardous waste as it is currently being generated and
facilitate the restoration of environmental conditions at traditional disposal sites;
3     provide for training and technology transfer, collaboration with foreign experts,
essential equipment and minor related infrastructure, studies and pilot and
demonstration projects.
2.           In general, it is intended that technical assistance activities will be directed at solving
problems, removing constraints and barriers, and strengthening institutions in the area of legislative
and regulatory policy reform. Technology and methodology improvements will include upgrading the
efficiency and operation of existing infrastructure, testing the application of new regulatory and
economic tools to improve enforcement and compliance, education and training, and strengthening and
streamlining administrative procedures and institutional arrangements.
3.           More specifically, the Ministry of Environmental Protection and Natural Resources
(MEPNR) and the World Bank have agreed on the following priorities related to the development of
specific activities within the Hazardous Waste Management Component:
*     Upgrading and developing environmental management infrastructure and institutions
for management of hazardous waste in the MEPNR and its associated agencies and
committees at the Republic, oblasts, kray, and local levels for management of
hazardous waste.
*     Carrying out of pilot projects and action in selected areas to enable the transfer and
adoption of modem approaches and technologies and to develop, test and demonstrate



152                                                       Environmental Management Project
new methodologies and approaches especially designed to reduce public exposure to
hazardous waste, minimize creation of new waste and reduce the volume of existing
stored waste and improve capacity in setting priorities for cleaning up existing
disposal sites.
4.            The predominant method of hazardous and industrial waste management is large scale
land disposal using unlined lagoons and landfills. Release of liquid industrial waste water, either
directly or via municipal sewers, is also widespread. Little formal treatment, resource recovery, or
waste minimization techniques are applied. Substantial quantities of waste are also being stored at
generating enterprises, pending the availability of adequate treatment and disposal facilities. There
is widespread illegal, indiscriminate, unauthorized dumping of industrial waste. Waste streams are
typically intermixed, thereby complicating treatment and disposal. Scarcity of land is putting pressure
on enterprises to consider options other than land disposal. Concern for surface water quality and
potential contamination of primary domestic and industrial water supplies is rising.
5.           MEPNR officials as well as those at the regional level believe that abatement and
remediation of the existing hazardous waste problems in Russia cannot proceed without specific
legislation dealing with hazardous waste and a strengthening of the supporting institutional system for
its management in accordance with well established "cradle to grave" principles. For their part,
MEPNR is actively developing a new set of laws applicable to waste management generally. They
are eager to apply relevant experience from other countries in enhancing and further developing the
specific legislative and institutional framework for hazardous waste. Similarity, they acknowledge the
need to move this experience to the regional level where it can be practically applied.
6.           The World Bank Missions on the Hazardous Waste Component have concurred with
the need for legislative development and institutional system building as a basis for addressing the
hazardous waste issue. More specifically, the observation has been made that the planning and
implementation of a comprehensive legislative and institutional framework suffeis from a lack of
current and complete data respecting hazardous waste generation and management practice. In
addition, an opportunity exists to integrate the development of this framework with current trends
toward waste prevention at source, and as a positive factor in the technological change and
modernization programs being undertaken in the nation's industrial sector.
7.           On this basis, two core subcomponents, of which this is one, have been identified for
the Environmental Management Project (EMP), Hazardous Waste Component. These are:
*     Development of a National Industrial Waste Data Management System
a     Development and Demonstration of Regulatory Management System for Hazardous
Waste Control at the Regional Level
8.           A third Subcomponent Project entitled the "Development and Demonstration of Waste
Related Environmental Management Studies" has also been developed under the overall EMP,
Hazardous Waste Component framework. This identifies six enterprise specific studies covering the
oil refining, steel making, metal fabricating, printing, paint manufacturing, and chemical sectors.
These are being presented as opportunities for donor countries who may participate in the EMP.
9.           The development of a legal and legislative framework for Hazardous Waste
Management, is included in the Regional Policy and Regulatory Support Component of EMP.



Annex 3.4.1                                                                            153
10.           This subcomponent project is the first of those listed above. A general observation
of the World Bank Missions on the Hazardous Waste Component of EMP is that there is a lack of an
adequate information base respecting the generation and disposition of industrial waste at the national
level. A consistent common basis for the consolidation and analysis of this information is also
required. This presents a significant impediment to policy development, and prioritizing coordinated
national response action, particularly with respect to the development of effective and viable waste
management infrastructure. The development of a national industrial waste data management system
and its demonstration as a planning tool for waste management facility planning is felt by both the
World Bank and MEPNR to be a high priority perquisite to effective action on the issue.
11.           A basic national waste classification system has been developed and implemented.
However, this has not been fully extended to the detailed level required for an effective regulatory
management system, nor has its review for consistency with the Basel Convention on the Control of
Transboundary Movements of Hazardous Wastes and their Disposal been completed. The Russian
Federation has signed but not formally ratified this international convention. Work to make the
necessary changes has been initiated but is not progressing expeditiously.
12.           A number of waste data collection initiatives have been undertaken at the local,
industrial sector and national levels. Under MEPNR direction, City and Oblast Environmental
Committee's have established reporting requirements for major enterprises in the last several years
and this information is being accumulated. However, the transfer of this information to and within
the federal level on a consistent basis is sporadic and incomplete. At the federal level, a national
waste inventory has been undertaken by the State Institute for Applied Ecology (SIAE). However,
barriers within the national government structure appear to exist for the transfer of current data, such
that this inventory is current and comprehensive. Within MEPNR, resources available to handle,
interpret and transfer the data received also remains limited. Plans to have the SIAE consolidate
locally supplied data into a national inventory on a regular basis have not been implemented due to
lack of resources. In addition, independent nationwide studies of industrial waste data have been
carried out in the project "Waste," administered by the Institute for Economic Problems for Nature
Management (IEPNM). Similarly, several industry specific organizations, either Ministries or
Committees for particular industrial sectors or associated Institutes, have data on wastes in their
particular industrial sectors. However, a general lack of coordination and consolidation of this
information has been noted and conflicts respecting valuation and access of this data are apparent.
13.          It has been observed that current industrial waste management practices depend almost
exclusively on direct land disposal, utilizing large scale lagoons and landfills, or direct discharge of
liquid effluents to surface water. Only limited discrimination among these industrial wastes is utilized
in employing these disposal practices. These practices are resulting in significant environmental
impact and in many cases have exhausted available land. A large scale development program will be
required to provide more effective and environmentally sound facilities, something that should involve
a nationally based plan, utilizing accurate data. In the absence of a consolidated picture of industrial
waste generation, tabulated on a consistent basis at the national level, it is difficult for coordinated
planning of actual waste management infrastructure to occur. As a result, initiatives currently being
proposed to MEPNR from the local and regional levels are largely being made on an adhoc basis.
14.           In summary, it has been concluded that the ability to quantify the amount, nature and
disposition of such wastes on a consistent basis across the country with any reliable accuracy is poor.
This creates a serious barrier to MEPNR being able to plan, prioritize and effectively implement waste
management legislative and regulatory programs on consistent national level. It also limits their ability
to rank problems, such that resources required for preventative and corrective action, particularly



154                                                      Environmental Management Project
related to new waste management infrastructure, can be allocated in an efficient manner. Finally, the
need to integrate hazardous waste management issues and impacts with air and water protection
programs and non-hazardous solid waste management initiatives is impeded. The latter is considered
a basic requirement for effective overall environmental policy decision making.
15.          This subcomponent project is intended to address these needs in both the near and long
term through the development of a national industrial waste data management and information system,
inclusive of providing a planning basis for new waste management infrastructure development. It is
seen as a necessary tool, required to support the Russian Federation's efforts to address it's hazardous
waste management problems.
B.    Objectives
16.          The overall objective of this subcomponent project is to provide the Russian Federation
and specifically MEPNR with the on going ability to collect, classify, document, analyze and report
data respecting the nature, quantity and disposition of industrial and particularly hazardous wastes
generated within the Federation.
17.          More specifically, an operational data management and information system is to be
developed for use within MEPNR for the purpose of defining industrial waste management issues and
support the development of effective national policies for the sound management of these wastes.
18.          Within three years, an operational data management system is to be in place, within
MEPNR. This system will allow accurate predictions of waste generation to be made, as a function
of waste type, industrial sector and region, and utilizing a uniform waste classification system
compatible with the Basel Convention. In addition, it will be utilized to initiate the coordinated
planning of improved waste management infrastructure at the national level during this period.
19.          All of this work shall be carried out in a manner contributing to the broader objectives
and priorities of the Environmental Management Project (EMP) and the  Hazardous Waste
Management Component. To this end, close coordination and integration of activities with other
subcomponent projects within the Hazardous Waste Management Component, and where appropriate
with the following EMP components:
*     Policy and Regulatory Support Component
*     Environmental Epidemiology Component
*     Water Quality Management Component
C.    Assistance Strategy
20.          The assistance provided for through this subcomponent project will extend for a three
year period, starting in November, 1994.
21.          Consistent with the objective of developing a continuing capability for the collection
and analysis of waste related information at the national level, this subcomponent project will be
implemented under the supervision of the Institute for Economic Problems for Nature Management
(IEPNM), an organization providing expert technical support to MEPNR. It is intended that the
capability and infrastructure developed, namely the National Industrial Waste Data Management
System, will be transferred to this organization upon the subcomponent project's completion for the
on going use by MEPNR.



Annex 3.4.1                                                                      155
22.          Direct supervision of the subcomponent project's implementation will be provided by
a Russian Project Manager, reporting to IEPNM. Staffing will be provided by Russian technical
professionals recruited primarily from local Institutes and other organizations, on the basis of a
secondment arrangement, such that a transfer of experience and expertise is assured upon the
subcomponent project's completion. Foreign advisor assistance in each of the subcomponent's
elements will be provided by a foreign consultant, contracted in accordance with the international
competitive bidding practices established for the EMP.
23.          The subcomponent project team will liaise closely with those undertaking other
projects within the Hazardous Waste Management Component of EMP, as well those being
undertaking in other EMP components. Facilitation of this liaison, as required, will be through the
Center for Project Preparation and Implementation (CPPI) and the supervisory committees established
within MEPNR.
24.          Training will form an important element of the subcomponent project with the transfer
of operational data management capability into IEPNM and MEPNR being a priority. This will most
effectively take place through close collaboration between the technical advisors, the Russian technical
professionals employed as part of the subcomponent project team, and IEPNM and MEPNR staff.
In addition, formal training events such as workshops, regular presentations, study tours and group
discussions should also be included. As appropriate, these training opportunities should be extended
to representatives of various industrial sectors affected by the work. Specific training will also be
coordinated with broader training activities undertaken with in other EMP components as appropriate.
D.    Counterparts and Implementation Arrangements
25.          The coordinating agency for this subcomponent project will be MEPNR and
specifically the Hazardous Waste Management Component Management Committee (HWMMC). The
HWMMC has been formed to provide overall supervision of the Hazardous Waste Management
Component and, under the Chairmanship of MEPNR, has representation from:
3     National Industrial Committees and Ministries
e     State Institute for Statistics
*     Ministry of Economy
*     Participating Oblast Environmental Committees
26.          The Center for Project Preparation and Implementation (CPPI), under the direction
of the Overall EMP Project Manager, will be responsible for project management, contractual,
financial, and routine administrative arrangements for the project as defined in the Terms of Reference
established for the operation of the CPPI in an Agreement between the MEPNR and CPPI.
27.          The Project's implementing agency will be the Institute of Economic Problems of
Nature Management (IEPNM) which operates as a supporting organization to the MEPNR and which
will report to the HWMMC.
28.          The Project will be organized under the direction of a Subcomponent Project Manager,
reporting to IEPNM, and responsible for direction of all local and foreign technical resources
assembled for the Project's implementation, and for support resources dedicated to or contracted by
the Project.



156                                                     Environmental Management Project
29.          Under the Subcomponent Project Manger, the Project will be organized in accordance
with its functional parts, namely:
*     Rapid Assessment of Existing Data
*     System Design, Development and Data Verification
*     Data Evaluation and System Implementation
30.          Each functional part identified above will be directed by a Task Manager, reporting
to the Subcomponent Project Manager, and who will be responsible for technical and support
resources dedicated to the specific part's implementation. Foreign technical advisors will be assigned
to each of the specific parts of the Project.
31.          A foreign consultant, known as the General Consultant reporting to the Overall EMP
Project Manager and having responsibility for subcomponent project start-up assistance and Project
monitoring for the EMP, Hazardous Waste Component, will provide advice and assistance to IEPNM
and Subcomponent Project Manager during the Project's start up period. This advice will cover the
areas of staff selection, terms of reference development for the overall work as well as those
applicable to the foreign consultant and Russian experts assigned to it, development of detailed work
plans, establishment of administrative procedures, budgeting, reporting, and project management
training. During Project implementation, the General Consultant will provide continuing advice to
the Subcomponent Project Manager and assist MEPNR to monitor and report on the Project's overall
performance and progress, on a quarterly basis.
32.          The Subcomponent Project Manager shall be selected on a competitive basis, consistent
with the procurement practices of the CPPI and World Bank involving at least three qualified Russian
candidates. The selection will be made by a selection committee represented by the CPPI, HWMMC
and
IEPNM. The selected Subcomponent Project Manager shall be employed under a contract with the
CPPI, such contract being subject to the approval of World Bank.
33.          Russian project staff will be recruited on a competitive basis. Where such expertise
is currently employed within the MEPNR, affiliated Institutes, Environmental Committees, and or
other government organizations, they will be seconded on the basis of taking a leave of absence
without compensation from their current positions for the period of their project assignments.
Employment will be covered by standard contracts with the CPPI, as provided for in the CPPI Terms
of Reference.
34.          Foreign Technical Advisers directly assigned to the subcomponent will be employed
through one consulting contract established through the overall EMP project procurement practice,
administered by the CPPI in accordance with its Terms of Reference, and involving an international
competitive bidding process. Selection of this consultant will be made by the IEPNM, HWMMC and
CPPI on the advice of the Subcomponent Project Manager and General Consultant.
35.          Technical services and expertise from Russian organizations other than IEPNM and
which may be required will be procured on a competitive basis and employed under contracts, either
directly with the CPPI or by the foreign consultant contracted for the supply of foreign technical
advisers.



Annex 3.4.1                                                                       157
36.          Procurement of computer, and specialized office support equipment and supplies shall
be undertaken through the CPPI in accordance with the overall EMP project procurement practices
based on international competitive bidding or such exceptions to this as approved by the World Bank.
37.          The subcomponent project will be headquartered and based in the IEPNM in Moscow.
Specific tasks may be based at other locations as determined by mutual agreement among the parties,
considering the practicality of effectively undertaking the specific work requirements at that location,
and the availability of suitable office, as well as the effective management and organization of the
subcomponent.
38.          Counterpart and implementation arrangements as described above, inclusive of a
functional organization structure, and various undertakings and commitments of the various parties
have been documented in a Framework Agreement between MEPNR, IEPNM and the CPPI. This
Agreement is included in Annex 7.7.4(a).
E.    Activities and Outputs
39.          This subcomponent project is directed toward the progressive development of a
national industrial waste data management system over a three year period. In the first year, all
existing data be consolidated, the revised national waste classification will be implemented and a
preliminary assessment of it will be undertaken. This will provide initial information for immediate
policy planning. During the second year, an automated data management system will be developed
and tested. Over the three year period, data analysis capability, specifically directed to its utilization
in the planning of waste management infrastructure will be developed and training in the system within
industry and local environment committees will be undertaken. The basic product is an operational
system within MEPNR at the end of this period. The three defined parts of the project are described
in more detail in the following.
Part 1:      Rapid Assessment
40.           This element will target the consolidation of existing data and implementation of
pending revisions to the national waste classification system. It's efficient completion is viewed as
a condition of continuing with subsequent project parts. lt should also provide a general consolidated
assessment of the current national picture respecting industrial waste generation and its disposition,
inclusive of storage for future treatment and disposal. An existing World Bank model, utilizing
industrial production statistics and factors may be employed, along with the consolidation of existing
data. Part 1 is expected to be completed by the end of Year 1 of the project and be an input into the
updating of the Russian National Environmental Action Plan (NEAP), which is being undertaken as
part of the National and Regional Policy and Regulatory Support Component.
40.           The following specific activities and outputs are identified as being required:
a)    Consolidation and review of all waste generation and disposition data currently in
MEPNR's hands.
b)    Identification of all other sources or repository of data within other Federal Ministries,
Committees or affiliated Institutes, regional Environment Committees and
Administrations and independent organizations.



158                                                         Environmental Management Project
c)     Removal of barriers to access to this data and establishment of mechanisms and
procedures for continued collection and transfer of it.
d)     Validation of the revised national waste classification as consistent with international
agreements and suitability for application at both national and local levels on an
ongoing basis.
e)    Implementation of the revised national waste classification system through Ministerial
action or equivalent means such that it is established as a national standard.
f)     Translation of existing data at a high level into the revised industrial waste
classification system and aggregation of this information in a report, describing the
waste type, geographical distribution of generation, industrial sector of generation and
disposition as a function of quantity.
g)     Review and apply as appropriate, the World Bank Model with particular reference to
available industrial production factors and other inputs.
h)     Develop formal reports respecting waste generation and its impacts for purposes of
inclusion into the Russian Environmental Action Plan.
Part 2:       System Design, Development and Data Verification
41.          This element will utilize the experience from Part 1 in the development of an automated
system for waste generation collection, consolidation and evaluation of data obtained by MEPNR on
an ongoing basis. This will entail physical development of a centralized data management system,
inclusive of hardware and software as well as establishment of procedures and practices necessary to
support it, both within MEPNR and at the regional and industrial enterprise level. Data verification
will be particularly important in this stage. This part is envisioned to begin during the overall
project's first year with a functioning system being in place and tested by the end of Year 2. The
following specific activities and outputs are identified as being required.
a)     Review data format and input requirements with the framework of the revised national
waste classification system.
b)     Identify and define the system's reporting requirements at all levels that it will serve.
c)     Undertake consultation with stakeholders providing inputs to or receiving information
from the system.
d)     Develop conceptual system design and architecture.
e)     Develop appropriate data management software and hardware specifications for the
system.
f)     Procurement or development of system hardware and software.
g)     Develop and test the system utilizing available data.



Annex 3.4. 1                                                                           159
h)     Develop, consult on and finalize procedures for use within MEPNR, regional
Environment Committees, and industry for data collection, reporting, consolidation and
application to the system.
i)     Develop data verification protocols applicable to the system.
j)     Document the system's design and operation in manual form  for transfer to
IEPNM/MEPNR's operating responsibility.
Part 3:       Data Evaluation and System Implementation
42.          This element involves the formal implementation of the system nationally and its
application to evaluate data for purposes of developing national industrial waste management policies
and action plans. With respect to the latter, specific emphasis will be placed on the use of information
generated as the system is developed to identify and prioritize requirements for waste management
facilities on a coordinated basis. It will also focus on the training and transfer aspects of the project
to ensure that the experience and system operation expertise is ultimately operational within
IEPNM/MEPNR and, as required, regional and industrial organizations. In particular, it will include
training at the waste generation data collection level to ensure consistency and improved data quality.
This part extends over the full three year project period. The following specific activities and outputs
are identified as being required.
a)     Rapid assessment evaluation of existing data with respect to potential generic options
for its treatment disposal.
b)     Preliminary prioritization of waste generation with respect to type and potential
environmental and heath impacts in consultation with Environmental Epidemiology
Component.
c)     Development of a national inventory of existing waste management facilities of all
types, along with a general assessment of their capacity and quality.
d)     Establishment of temporary guidelines for the development of new facilities consistent
with the above preliminary evaluation.
e)     Update waste management infrastructure planing and guidelines as additional data
becomes available from the system.
f)     Undertake consultation with regional authorities and industry on implementation of
national waste management infrastructure development guidelines and finalize these for
implementation.
g)     Develop training plans in use of the system inclusive of identification of resource
requirements within IEPNM, MEPNR and regional agencies.
h)     Undertake training of system operating staff and others at the regional and industrial
level with emphasis on ensuring consistent and accurate data is being collected at its
source.



160                                                      Environmental Management Project
i)    Coordinate these activities with the Regulatory Management System for Hazardous
Waste Control at the Regulatory Level subcomponent project being pursued in parallel
such that the national industrial waste data management system and infrastructure
planning work is consistent with the detailed hazardous waste classification and tracking
systems, and facility approval standards being developed in the other subcomponent.
F.   Reporting
43.         The Subcomponent Project Manager will submit a series of regular progress reports
as well as formal reports at project milestones and an overall report upon completion of each part.
All reports shall be available to IEPNM, the Hazardous Waste Management Component Management
Committee, the CPPI, and World Bank. Four Russian language and two English language copies shall
be submitted to IEPNM. Eight Russian language and two English language copies shall be submitted
to the Hazardous Waste Management Component Management Committee. Two English language
copies shall be submitted to the World Bank. Four Russian language and four English language copies
shall be forwarded to the CPPI.
44.         Regular progress reports are anticipated to be in the form of informal briefs presented
at least tri-yearly and cover the following:
*     Description of activities in the reporting period
*     Contributions to Project objectives
*     Progress in relation to the established work plans
*     Budget reporting including forecasts and commitment schedules
*     Problems encountered and remedies sought or proposed
*     Activities anticipated in the coming period
45.         The following summarizes the anticipated formal reporting requirements based on a
thirty six (36) month schedule:
Part 1: Rapid Assessment
Interim Technical Report                 Month 6
Final Technical Report                   Month 12
Part 2: System Design. Development and Data Verification
Interim Technical Reports                Months 18
Final System Design Report               Month 24
Part 3: Data Evaluation and System Implementation
Interim Technical Reports                Month 12, 24
Final Technical Report                   Month 36
46.         As part of the Subcomponent Project's start up activities and with the assistance of the
General Consultant, detailed reporting procedures will be established.



Annex 3.4.1                                                                        161
G.  Foreign Consultant Qualifications
47.         The selected foreign consultant, including any subcontractors, should offer the following
specialties and experience:
*     Experience with the development of national level hazardous waste inventories in
industrialized countries.
*     Familiarity with industrial and hazardous waste management infrastructure planning and
policy development.
*     Broad exposure to industrial production technology and processes in a range of key
industrial sectors.
*     Experience with modelling of industrial economies and their performance.
*     Strong data management and system development capability.
*     Project management experience with major study projects in the Russian Federation,
C.I.S. and/or Central Europe.
*     Availability of Russian expertise in some or all of the above areas.
48.         Russian language capability of individual team members will greatly enhance their
effectiveness and will therefore play an important role in selection of the foreign consultant.



SrAFF APPRAISAL REPORT
RUSSIAN FEDERATION
ENVlRONMNENTAL MANAGEMENT PIOECT
ANNEX 3.4.2
REGULATORY MANAGEMENT SYSTEM
FOR HAZARDOUS WASTE CONTROL AT THE REGIONAL LEVEL
SUBCOMPONENT DESCRIPTION
A.  Background
1.           This subcomponent project is one of two core subcomponents to be executed by the
Russian Federation as part of the Environmental Management Project (EMP), Hazardous Waste
Component. The purpose of the Hazardous Waste Component is to provide key elements of technical
assistance to the Russian Federation at the national and regional level in their efforts to:
*     prevent the further build-up of hazardous wastes which pose a health threat to
workers, the population at large, and threaten the economic viability of enterprises
over the longer term;
     develop programs for prevention of formation (where possible) and\or recycle or re-
use of hazardous wastes;
=     improve the management of hazardous waste as it is currently being generated and
facilitate the restoration of environmental conditions at traditional disposal sites;
3     provide for training and technology transfer, collaboration with foreign experts,
essential equipment and minor related infrastructure, studies and pilot and
demonstration projects.
2.           In general, it is intended that technical assistance activities will be directed at solving
problems, removing constraints and barriers, and strengthening institutions in the area of legislative
and regulatory policy reform. Technology and methodology improvements will include upgrading the
efficiency and operation of existing infrastructure, testing the application of new regulatory and
economic tools to improve enforcement and compliance, education and training, and strengthening and
streamlining administrative procedures and institutional arrangements.
3.           More specifically, the Ministry of Environmental Protection and Natural Resources
(MEPNR) and the World Bank have agreed on the following priorities related to the development of
specific activities within the Hazardous Waste Management Component:
*     Upgrading and developing environmental management infrastructure and institutions
for the management of hazardous waste in the MEPNR and its associated agencies and
committees at the Republic, oblasts, kray, and local levels.
*     Carrying out of pilot projects and action in selected areas to enable the transfer and
adoption of modem approaches and technologies and to develop, test and demonstrate
new methodologies and approaches especially designed to reduce public exposure to



Annex 3.4.2                                                                       163
hazardous waste, minimize creation of new waste and reduce the volume of existing
stored waste and improve capacity in setting priorities for cleaning up existing
disposal sites.
4.           The predominant method of hazardous and industrial waste management is large scale
land disposal using unlined lagoons and landfills. Release of liquid industrial waste water, either
directly or via municipal sewers, is also widespread. Little formal treatment, resource recovery, or
waste minimization techniques are applied. Substantial quantities of waste are also being stored at
generating enterprises, pending the availability of adequate treatment and disposal facilities. There
is widespread illegal, indiscriminate, unauthorized dumping of industrial waste. Waste streams are
typically intermixed, thereby complicating treatment and disposal. Scarcity of land is putting pressure
on enterprises to consider options other than land disposal. Concern for surface water quality and
potential contamination of primary domestic and industrial water supplies is rising.
5.           MEPNR officials as well as those at the regional level believe that abatement and
remediation of the existing hazardous waste problems in Russia cannot proceed without specific
legislation dealing with hazardous waste and a strengthening of the supporting institutional system for
its management in accordance with well established "cradle to grave" principles. For their part,
MEPNR is actively developing a new set of laws applicable to waste management generally. They
are eager to apply relevant experience from other countries in enhancing and further developing the
specific legislative and institutional framework for hazardous waste. Similarity, they acknowledge the
need to move this experience to the regional level where it can be practically applied.
6.           The World Bank Missions on the Hazardous Waste Component have concurred with
the need for legislative development and institutional system building as a basis for addressing the
hazardous waste issue. More specifically, the observation has been made that the planning and
implementation of a comprehensive legislative and institutional framework suffers from a lack of
current and complete data respecting hazardous waste generation and management practice. In
addition, an opportunity exists to integrate the development of this framework with current trends
toward waste prevention at source, and as a positive factor in the technological change and
modernization programs being undertaken in the nation's industrial sector.
7.           On this basis, two core subcomponents, of which this is one, have been identified for
the Environmental Management Project (EMP), Hazardous Waste Component. These are:
*     Development of a National Industrial Waste Data Management System
*     Development and Demonstration of Regulatory Management System for Hazardous
Waste Control at the Regional Level
8.           A third Subcomponent Project entitled the "Development and Demonstration of Waste
Related Environmental Management Studies" has also been developed under the overall EMP,
Hazardous Waste Component framework. This identifies six enterprise specific studies covering the
oil refining, steel making, metal fabricating, printing, paint manufacturing, and chemical se'tors.
These are being presented as opportunities for donor countries who may participate in the EMP.
9.           The development of a legal and legislative framework for Hazardous Waste
Management, is included in the National and Regional Policy and Regulatory Support Component
Institutional and Policies Component of EMP.



164                                                        Environmental Management Project
10.          This subcomponent project is the second of the above listed core subcomponent
projects. It is directed toward the creation of the basic regulatory system necessary to provide for the
detailed characterization and tracking of hazardous wastes, and to control the management of these
wastes. Such a system is considered a fundamental requirement for dealing with the hazardous waste
problem and developing improved management practices. This has been reinforced by the conclusions
of the World Bank Legal Team who recommend that the development of functional environmental
control regulations should take priority over the actual laws which will eventually provide a legal
framework for their application.
11.          Two approaches are available to developing and implementing this functional
regulatory management capability. It could be developed at the national level and passed down to
regional Environment Committees for implementation. Alternatively, it could be developed, tested
and demonstrated within a representative regional jurisdiction or group of regional jurisdictions. It
would then be adopted for broader national application under the auspices of the MEPNR. The former
approach is institutionally difficult to do at this time and likely beyond the current resources available.
The latter approach will yield more immediate, tangible results and optimize the use of available
resources.
12.          Oblast and City Environmental Committees have generally made some progress in
identifying where hazardous waste are generated and, to a lesser degree, what is happening to them.
To date, activity seems to have focused primarily on quantifying generation at major industries,
largely as a basis for determining pollution fee assessments. However, they have not had the resources
to develop or implement any but the most rudimentary regulatory mechanisms or practices required
to exercise control over its generation, or disposition, inclusive of its storage pending availability of
proper management facilities.
13.          The basic requirements commonly identified as necessary for an effective hazardous
waste regulatory system are the ability to characterize and classify the wastes, track them from point
of generation through to their final disposal, and control the methods applied to their management.
More specifically, three fundamental regulatory system components are required:
*     Detailed Hazardous Waste Classification System
*     Hazardous Waste Tracking System
*     Hazardous Waste Management Facility Approval System
14.          Each of these system components will consist of a number of elements, including
formal enforceable regulations, implementation procedures, communication and consultation practice
on their implementation, and training for both regulatory officials and those to whom the system is
applied. It is understood that the overall waste classification system, currently under development
within MEPNR, will be finalized and enacted as a priority task within the National Industrial Waste
Data Management System Subcomponent Project. Within this subcomponent project, the waste
classification system will be implemented at a detailed level.
15.          In order to adequately support the implementation of this system, it is recognized that
a physical measurement capability in the form of analytical, sampling and monitoring services is also
required to characterize wastes and evaluate the environmental performance of management practices
applied to it. Therefore, the enhancement of existing regional measurement capability should be
provided for and integrated with the regulatory system's development.



Annex 3.4.2                                                                       165
16.          This subcomponent project will be executed at a regional level, recognizing a role
must be played by national authorities to ensure the experience is transierred to other regions. A
number of regional jurisdictions were jointly assessed by MEPNR and World Bank Missions as
candidates for this project. This assessment involved evaluation of present local regulatory capacity
as reflected in the Oblast and City Environment Committees, commitment to addressing the issue
exhibited by regional and local councils and administrations, the nature and distribution of hazardous
waste problems requiring attention, and the practicality of an area serving as an effective
demonstration to others at the regional level.
17.          On the basis of this assessment, two Oblasts, namely Yaroslavl and Vologda in the
Upper Volga region have been selected. A high level of commitment and cooperation is exhibited by
the regional and local Environment Committees, particularly within the major industrial centers of
Yaroslavl and Cherepovetz. Local administrations and elected Councils appear willing to take the
necessary action to support a regional regulatory control system. The area offers a wide distribution
of representative industry which will be characteristic of their respective industrial sectors. Significant
industrial and hazardous waste problems have already been identified in the area, some of which are
considered critical in environmental impact terms, particularly in relation to the Volga River and
Ribinsk Reservoir. Finally, several other EMP Components which will be complimentary are slated
for implementation in the Region. These include three potential waste related environmental studies
identified as donor funded technical assistance opportunities as part of the Hazardous Waste
Component (Cherepovetz Steel Mill, Yaroslavl Paint and Refinery enterprises). A subcomponent of
the Water Quality Management Component will be done in the Upper Volga Region. A regional
subcomponent project has been identified for the City of Cherepovetz as part of the Environmental
Epidemiology Subcomponent. Finally, the project will be supported by the National and Regional
Regulatory Support Component.
B.    Objectives
18.          The overall objective of this subcomponent project is to develop and demonstrate the
basic elements of a functional regulatory capability, necessary to control the generation and
management of hazardous waste, at a regional level. More specifically, it is intended to develop and
put in place the necessary tools, in the form of regulations, practices, procedures and support
infrastructure, which can effectively:
*     characterize and classify hazardous wastes for regulatory control purposes;
*     track hazardous wastes from point of their source of generation to point of disposal;
*     control the management practices applied to them throughout their life cycle: and
*     provide sufficient measurement capability to adequately support the above capability.
19.          All of this work will be carried out in a manner contributing to the broader objectives
and priorities of the Environmental Management Project (EMP) and its Hazardous Waste Component.
To this end, close coordination and integration of activities with other subcomponent projects within
the Hazardous Waste Component, and, where appropriate, with other EMP Components as follows:
*     Policy and Regulatory Support Component
*     Environmental Epidemiology Component
*     Water Quality Management Component



166                                                     Environmental Management Project
C.    Assistance Strategy
20.          The assistance proposed under this project will extend over a four year period, starting
in November, 1994.
21.          Consistent with the objective of developing and demonstrating basic regulatory
management capability at the regional level, this subcomponent project will be implemented under the
supervision of a Regional Committee chaired by the Oblast Environmental Committees and having
representation by key stakeholder groups as listed in Section D below.
22.          Direct supervision of the subcomponent project's implementation will be provided by
a Russian Subcomponent Project Manager, reporting to the Regional Committee. Staffing will be
provided by Russian technical professionals recruited from related Government organizations such as
Environmental Committees and Administrations, local Institutes and other organizations within the
region. Employment will be on the basis of a secondment arrangement, such that a transfer of
experience and expertise is assured upon the subcomponent project's completion. Foreign advisor
assistance in each of the subcomponent's elements will be provided a foreign consultant, contracted
in accordance with the international competitive bidding practices established for the EMP.
23.          The subcomponent project team will liaise closely with those undertaking other
subcomponent projects within the EMP Hazardous Waste Management Component as well those being
undertaken in other EMP Components, particularly those with Regional subcomponents focused in the
Upper Volga Region. Facilitation of this liaison as required will be provided by the Center for Project
Preparation and Implementation (CPPI) and the various supervisory committees established within
MEPNR.
24.          Training will form an important element of the subcomponents project. This will most
effectively take place through close collaboration between the technical advisors, the Russian technical
professionals employed as part of the project team, MEPNR officials and the regulatory staff in the
regional and city authorities.  In addition, formal training events such as workshops, regular
presentations, study tours and group discussions should also be included.  As appropriate, these
training opportunities should be  extended to regional industries affected by the project's
implementation, other affected agencies in the Upper Volga Region, and regional stakeholders such
as non-government organization, the media, and members of the public. Project specific training will
also be coordinated with broader EMP training initiatives undertaken under other EMP components
as appropriate.
25.          Public and stakeholder consultation on the regulatory system under development will
be required. It is considered critical to the project's success that a consensus on the system among
a wide range of affected parties be achieved as a basis for the system's implementation, demonstration
and ultimately effective adoption as a model for wider application in the Russian Federation.
D.    Counterparts and Implementation Arrangements
26.          The coordinating agency for this subcomponent project will be MEPNR and
specifically the Hazardous Waste Management Component Management Committee (HWMMC). This
Committee has been formed to provide overall supervision of the Hazardous Waste Management
Component and, under the Chairmanship of MEPNR, has representation from:



Annex 3.4.2                                                                      167
*     National Industrial Committees and Ministries
*     State Institute for Statistics
*     Ministry of Economy
*     Participating Oblast Environmental Committees
27.          The Center for Project Preparation and Implementation (CPPI), under the direction
of the Overall EMP Project Manager, will be responsible for overall project management, contractual,
financial, and routine administrative arrangements for the project as defined in the Terms of Reference
established for the operation of the CPPI in an Agreement between the MEPNR and CPPI.
28.          The Project's implementing agency will be a regional management committee, known
as the Regional Hazardous Waste Regulatory Project Management Committee, which is referred to
herein as the Committee. The Committee will be established under the auspices of the Inter-Regional
Upper Volga Environmental Council and report to the overall EMP Hazardous Waste Management
Component Management Committee (HWMMC) established within the MEPNR.
29.          Chairmanship of the Committee will be shared on a rotating basis by the Oblast
Environmental Committee Chairman from Vologda and Yaroslavl, or their delegates. Membership
on the Committee shall include but not be limited to representatives of:
: Oblast Administrations
*     Cherepovetz and other City Environmental Committees
Ministry of Environmental Protection and Natural Resources
3     Major Regional Industries
i     Environmental Organization Representatives
3     Regional Technical Institutes

reporting to the Committee and be responsible for direction of all local and foreign technical resources
assembled for the Project's implementation, and for support resources dedicated or contracted to the
Project.

functional parts, namely:
*     Waste Classification
*     Waste Management Facility Standards
*     Waste Tracking System

Project Manager or Task Manager, reporting to the Project Manager, and who shall be responsible
for technical resources dedicated to the specific parts's implementation.
33.          Foreign technical advisors will be assigned to specific parts with an additional senior
foreign technical advisor assigned to assist the Subcomponent Project Manager with both technical and
project management matters and coordinate the activities of other foreign technical advisors assigned
to specific parts of the Project.
