35.          The Subcomponent Project Manager will be selected on a competitive basis, consistent
with the procurement practices of the CPPI and World Bank involving at least three qualified Russian
candidates. The selection will be made by a selection committee represented by the CPPI, HWMMC
and the Committee. The selected Subcomponent Project Manager will be employed under a contract
with the CPPI, such contract being subject to the approval of World Bank.
36.          Russian project staff will be recruited to the maximum degree possible from qualified
technical expertise resident in the region, on a competitive basis. Where such expertise is currently
employed within the Oblast and City Administrations, Environmental Committees, local Institutes and
any other Goverrnent organizations, they shall be seconded to the Project on the basis of taking a
leave of absence for the period of their Project assignments, without compensation from their current
positions. Employment will be covered by standard contracts with the Committee, established on the
basis of delegated authority from the CPPI, as provided for in the CPPI Terms of Reference.
37.          Foreign Technical Advisers directly assigned to the Project will be employed through
one consulting contract established through the overall EMP project procurement practice,
administered by the CPPI in accordance with its Terms of Reference, and involving an international
competitive bidding process. Selection of this consultant will be made by Committee, HWMMC and
CPPI on the advice of the Subcomponent Project Manager and General Consultant.
38.          Technical services and expertise from Russian organizations that may be required will
be procured on a competitive subcontracted basis, either directly with the Committee or by the foreign
consultant contracted for the supply of foreign technical advisers. All such arrangements are subject
to the approval of the CPPI and World Bank.
39.          Procurement of computer, specialized office support equipment and supplies, and
laboratory equipment shall be undertaken through the CPPI in accordance with the overall EMP
project procurement practices based on international competitive bidding or such exceptions to this as
approved by the World Bank.
40.          The Project will be headquartered and based in Yaroslavl, subject to the availability
of suitable office space to be supplied by the Oblast or Regional administrations. Specific Project
tasks may be based at other locations in the region as determined by mutual agreement among the
parties, considering the practicality of effectively undertaking the specific work requirements at that
location, and the availability of suitable office and living accommodation for project staff and technical
advisors during project assignments, as well as the effective management and organization of the
Project.



Annex 3.4.2                                                                       169
41.          Laboratory facilities selected for upgrading will be those currently operated by the
Oblast and/or City Environmental Committees at one location in each of Vologda and Yaroslavl
Oblasts.  Final selection of the upgraded laboratory locations will be a specific task of the
Measurement Capability part of the project, giving consideration to existing capability and resources,
and proximity to major regulated enterprises and waste management facilities.
42.          Counterpart and implementation arrangements as described above, inclusive of a
functional organization structure, and various undertakings and commitments of the various parties
have been documented in a Framework Agreement between MEPNR, the Committee and the CPPI.
E.    Activities and Outputs
43.          The overall scope of this subcomponent project is the development and implementation
of the three basic elements of a hazardous waste regulatory system, namely a detailed waste
classification system, a waste tracking system and a waste management facility approval system. This
will be done at the regional level in Vologda and Yaroslavl Oblasts with the full participation of
appropriate City Environment Committees, particularly in Cherepovetz and Yaroslavl.  Once
established it is intended to be emulated by other regions under the auspices of MEPNR. Recognizing
that such a system requires a measurement capability in the form of analytical, sampling and
monitoring capability to support it, upgrading of this type of infrastructure at the regional level will
be provided for in both Oblasts.
44.          The project has three Parts as follows:
Part 1 Detailed Waste Classification and Facility Standards Development
Part 2 Development and Implementation of a Hazardous Waste Tracking System
Part 3 Establishment of a Supporting Measurement Capability
45.          Part 1 will undertake the development and implementation of two regulatory
management elements; detailed waste classification and facility standards. Part 2 will be directed
toward development and implementation of the actual waste tracking system. Both Parts 1 and 2 will
have a number of common generic tasks, these being the development of enforceable regulations, the
development of implementation procedures related to such things as interpretation, enforcement,
reporting, and training. Part 3, involving the development of measurement capability, will also have
strong emphasis on training, and as well as applicable testing and QA/QC standards. In all cases,
consistency with international standards and agreements will be a consideration. Similarly, each part
will require specific stakeholder consultation during system development and communication during
its implementation.
Part 1:      Waste Classiflcation System and Facility Standards Development.
46.           This element will cover the following scope, activity and output elements:
ScpRe:
1.    Evaluate the regulatory measures proposed with respect to their economic impact and
cost benefit to ensure their practicality.



170                                                        Environmental Management Project
2.    Implement and test a detailed hazardous waste classification system which, in effect,
will act as the common language and definition base for the regulatory system,
utilizing the national waste classification system finalized as part of the National
Industrial Waste Data Management System subcomponent project.
3.     Ensure that this system can be practically applied in the Russian context, adequately
prioritizes potential environmental risk and impact, supports the requirements of the
other regulatory system elements, and is compatible with various international
standards and agreements that the country is or may be signatory to.
4.     Develop an effective regulatory control capability for the various waste management
activities applied to hazardous waste at various stages of their life cycle in the form
of licensing or permitting of specific activities or facilities required for their
management.
5.     Develop and implement of the necessary the procedures and practices required to
monitor the operation and environmental performance of these management activities
and facilities.
Activities and Outputs:
Task 1 Detailed Waste Classification
a)    In association with MEPNR, define the detailed requirements for an enhanced waste
classification system based on the national system developed as part of the National
Industrial Waste Data Management System subcomponent project.
b)     Prepare a draft detailed hazardous waste classification system  document for
stakeholder review.
c)     Undertake a consultation program  on the draft system  with a broad range of
stakeholders, including other regional and local authorities and governments, senior
governments, industry, non-government organizations, appropriate institutes and
academics, and international standards organizations.
d)     Finalize the system and, as applicable, present it for provisional adoption by the
appropriate regional elected body in a form having legal application on a trial basis.
e)     Undertake a program of communication and training on the system with key users,
particularly regulatory officials and industry personnel.
f)     Develop the necessary implementation procedures and practices, including testing
standards, documentation requirements, information management system requirements,
and guidelines for interpretation and decision making associated with the system's
application.
g)     Support the system's formal implementation in association with the development and
implementation of Part 2 (Waste Tracking System).



Annex 3.4.2                                                                          171
h)     Ensure coordination of analytical aspects of the classification system with the
upgrading of measurement capability undertaken in Part 3 (Measurement Capability).
i)    Assist in the transfer of the detailed waste classification system to MEPNR for
adoption as a national standard as appropriate.
Task 2 Facility Standards Development
a)     Review existing requirements for approval of hazardous waste management activities,
along with those in other comparable countries, and those that may be dictated by
international agreements.
b)    Recommend on the range of existing and potential hazardous waste management
activities and facilities to which a licensing and monitoring regulatory system would
appropriately apply, inclusive of various management activities such as storage,
handling, treatment, land disposal, resource recovery and recycling, both at the source
of generation and elsewhere.
c)     Develop a draft approvals process for the evaluation and granting of permits or
licenses applicable to specific hazardous waste management operations, either existing
or proposed, and including such aspects as the general information requirements to
be supplied, public disclosure, consultation and review requirements, regulatory
decision making, and conditioning of approvals.
d)     Review existing Russian standards for hazardous waste management activities and
facilities, along with those applied internationally and as may be mandated by
appropriate international agreements.
e)     Develop draft standards and guidelines applicable to specific types of activities,
including such things as facility siting criteria, design standards, environmental
performance monitoring, operations and maintenance standards, and closure
provisions.
f)     Undertake a consultation program  covering the draft approval process and
management facility standards with a broad range of stakeholders, including other
regional and local authorities and governments, senior governments, industry, and
non-government organizations.
g)     Test the draft approval process and standards as applicable on one or more existing
local facilities.
h)     Finalize the regulatory requirements covering the application, approval process and
standards for hazardous waste management activities and facilities, and, as applicable,
present them for provisional adoption by the appropriate regional elected body in a
form having legal application on a trial basis.



172                                                       Environmental Management Project
i)    Develop implementation practices and procedures for these regulatory requirements
with particular emphasis on enforcement and monitoring of environmental
performance.
j)     Develop and deliver appropriate training programs to regulatory staff and industry as
required on the approval process, facility standards and the implementation
procedures.
k)    Assist in the transfer of these regulatory requirements to MEPNR for development as
national requirements, particularly in regards to the national waste management
facilities planning and guideline development being undertaken in the National
Industrial Waste Data Management System subcomponent project.
Part 2:      Development and Implementation of a Hazardous Waste Tracking System.
47.          This element will cover the following scope, activity and output elements:
Scope:
1 .    Design, develop and implement a capability at the regional level to monitor the
progression of hazardous waste from its point of generation, through any or all
management steps applied to it, its movement from one location to another, and to its
ultimate disposition.
2.    Ensure that this "Cradle to Grave" tracking capability will be suitable for determining
detailed estimates of the quantity and nature of waste production, to control the
activities employed in its management, to prioritize actions for improving management
and to determine its fate and environmental impact.
3.    Develop the system  in the form of regulations and implementation procedures
covering three fundamental elements: waste generator registration and reporting
requirements, the documentation and reporting requirements for waste movement,
processing and disposition, and requirements for reporting and responding to
contingency events associated with waste management activities.
Activities and Outputs:
Task I Waste Generator Registration System
a)    Review  requirements and practices in other relevant countries respecting the
mandatory identification of hazardous waste generation sources, their registration, and
associated waste generation documentation and reporting requirements.
b)     Develop a draft hazardous waste generator registration regulation.



Annex 3.4.2                                                                       173
c)    Develop draft practices and procedures covering implementation of generator
registration, including enforcement procedures, waste audit standards, applicability to
on-site management activities, and guidelines and reporting procedures.
d)    Develop a list of major generators to whom the requirements will apply.
e)    Undertake a consultation program on the draft system with a broad range of
stakeholders, including other regional and local authorities and governments, senior
governments, industry, and non-government organizations.
f)    Test the registration procedures on one or more major waste generators.
g)    Finalize the waste generator registration program and, as applicable, present it for
provisional adoption by the appropriate regional elected body in a form having legal
application on a trial basis.
h)    Undertake a program of communication and training on the system with key users,
particularly regulatory officials and industry personnel, and including guidance in
performing waste audits.
i)    Develop appropriate data management capability to collect and report information
producdd by the generator registration program and ensure its compatibility with the
national hazardous waste data management system under development in parallel with
this project.
j)     Develop and advise on the implementation of enforcement procedures.
k).    Ensure coordination of the registration program with other elements of the waste
tracking system (Part 2), detailed classification and management facility licensing (Part
1) and the upgrading of measurement capability undertaken (Part 3).
I)    Assist in the transfer of the waste generator registration program to MEPNR for
adoption and implementation as a national standard.
Task 2 Waste Movement Monitoring System
a)    Review regulatory standards covering the monitoring of hazardous waste movement
from source through to final disposition.
b)    Review the requirements respecting the movement of hazardous waste as set out in
applicable international protocols and agreements.
c)    Design and draft regulatory requirements providing for the documentation of
hazardous waste movements utilizing a manifest or comparable method.
d)    Review and recommend on the methodology and practices applicable to transportation
vehicle marking.



174                                                        Environmental Management Project
e)     Develop regulatory requirements applicable to qualification and licensing of hazardous
waste transportation.
f)     Undertake a consultation program  on the draft waste movement monitoring
requirements with a broad range of stakeholders, including other regional and local
authorities and governments, senior governments, industry, transportation services and
non-government organizations.
g)     Finalize the regulatory requirements covering hazardous waste movement monitoring
and transportation and, as applicable, present them for provisional adoption by the
appropriate regional elected body in a form having legal application on a trial basis.
h)     Undertake a program of communication and training on the system with key users,
particularly regulatory officials, industry personnel and transporters, including the
development and delivery of transportation operator training courses.
i)     Develop appropriate data management capability to collect and report information
produced from application of this system and ensure its compatibility with the
National Hazardous Waste Data Management System under development in parallel
with this subcomponent project.
j)     Develop and advise on the implementation of enforcement procedures as applied to
waste generators and transporters.
k).    Ensure coordination of the waste movement regulatory development with other
elements of the overall the waste tracking system (Task 1), the detailed waste
classification and management facility licensing (Part 1) and the upgrading of
measurement capability undertaken (Part 3).
I)     Assist in the transfer of the waste movement monitoring capability to MEPNR for
adoption and implementation as a national standard.
Task 3 Contingency Planning
a)     Develop draft regulatory requirements for spill and accident reporting related to
hazardous waste management activities.
b)     Develop draft spill and accident response plans.
c)     Undertake a consultation program on the draft spill and accident draft regulatory and
response requirements with a broad range of stakeholders, including other regional
and local authorities and governments, senior governments, industry, transportation
services and non-government organizations.
d)     Finalize the regulatory requirements covering spill and accident reporting and, as
applicable, present them for provisional adoption by the appropriate regional elected
body in a form having legal application on a trial basis.



Annex 3.4.2                                                                          175
e)     Develop implementation practices and procedures for the implementation of a spill and
accident response plan.
f)    Identify additional equipment and infrastructure support required for implementation
of the response plan.
g)     Undertake a program of communication and training on the system with key users,
particularly regulatory officials, industry personnel and transporters and including
organization of a trained response team.
h)     Assist in the transfer of the spill and accident reporting and response requirements to
MEPNR for integration with national requirements in this area.
Part 3:       Establishment of a Supporting Measurement Capability.
48.           This element will cover the following scope, activity and output elements:
Scope:
1.    Provide for the upgrading and additional development of local measurement capability
necessary to support the basic regulatory framework provided by the hazardous waste
characterization, tracking, and management facility approvals systems, through the
enhancement of analytical capability in the form of laboratory infrastructure and
associated sampling and environmental performance monitoring requirements.
2.     Undertake this task in two phases, the first being the development of a measurement
capability upgrading plan and the second being its implementation, inclusive of
training in two regional Environment Committee Laboratories, one in each of Vologda
and Yaroslavl Oblasts.
Activities and Outputs:
Task 1 Develop Measurement Capability Upgrading Plan
a)    Evaluate existing laboratory, sampling and environmental monitoring capability
offered by the local authorities inclusive of procedures, QA/QC standards, staff
qualifications and operating efficiency.
b)    Inventory and evaluate available laboratory, sampling and environmental monitoring
capability within regional or accessible national institutions and institutes as above.
c)    Inventory and evaluate laboratory, sampling and environmental monitoring capability
within key client industries as above.
d)     Define and document overall measurement capability requirements and needs, with
specific reference to those required to support the other regulatory components being
developed within this project, and the assessment of past practice impacts.



176                                                     Environmental Management Project
e)    In consultation with the HWMMC and Committee agency, select two laboratory
installations, one in each participating Oblast, that would be upgraded.
f)    Identify and specify specific equipment additional requirements for each location.
g)    Identify and scope practice and procedure enhancement requirements.
h)    Document and present for approval an overall measurement infrastructure upgrading
plan, inclusive of costs, implementation activities and schedule, and human resource
requirements.
Task 2 Implement Measurement Capabity Upgrading Plan
a)    Acquire and install equipment additions.
b)    Develop and implement enhanced operational practices and procedures.
c)    Install and test enhanced data management/reporting capability
d)    Establish appropriate QA/QC systems.
e)    Train personnel as required.
f)    Undertake certification of laboratory capability in accordance with recognized
standards.
F.    Reporting
49.          The Subcomponent Project Manager will submit a series of regular progress reports
as well as formal reports at project milestones and an overall report upon completion of each part.
All reports shall be available to the Committee, HWMMC, CPPI, and World Bank. Four Russian
language and two English language copies shall be submitted to the Committee. Eight Russian
language and two English language copies shall be submitted to the HWMMC. Two English language
copies shall be submitted to the World Bank. Four Russian language and four English language copies
shall be forwarded to the CPPI.
50.          Regular progress reports are anticipated to be in the form of informal briefs presented
at least tri-yearly and cover the following:
*     Description of activities in the reporting period
*     Contributions to Project objectives
*     Progress in relation to the established work plans
*     Budget reporting including forecasts and commitment schedules
*     Problems encountered and remedies sought or proposed
*     Activities anticipated in the coming period

ANNEX 4.1
NATIONAL POLLUTION ABATEMENT FACILITY
ASSUMPTIONS USED FOR FINANCIAL PROJECTIONS
The main assumptions used in the base case financial projections are as follows:
*     The NPAF lending rate is 11 percent;
The NPAF receives a grant of 10 million Swiss Francs (approximately $7 million);
*     The NPAF's weighted average cost of funds, including the Swiss grant, is 6.47
percent;
*     The average loan size is $1.9 million. The NPAF finances 30 projects with its initial
$50 million allocation from the Bank and $7 million grant from the Swiss
Government;
*     The initial $57 million allocation is committed over 3 years, at a pace of 10
commitments per year;
*     Sub-loans disburse over three calendar years -- 25 percent during the second semester
of the first year, 50 percent during the second year, and 25 percent during the first
semester of the third year;
*     Sub-loans are repaid in 8 equal, semi-annual installments starting at the beginning of
the fourth year and ending in the second half of the seventh year;
*     All principal repayments received by the NPAF are relent by the NPAF to new
borrowers so that the loan portfolio remains constant at $50 million following the
initial start-up phase;
*     The NPAF charges an up-front appraisal fee of 1 percent of the loan commitment or
$16,666 for the average loan and an annual supervisory fee of 0.25 percent of the
outstanding balance of each sub-loan;
*     Interest on sub-loans, appraisal fees, and supervisory fees constitute the only sources
of income for the NPAF;



180                                                        Environmental Management Project
*     70 percent of all net income is retained by the NPAF and used to finance additional
sub-loans on the same terms and conditions as the initial sub-loans; the remaining 30
percent of net income is transferred to the Ministry of Finance;
*     NPAF expenses consist of the following items;
A commitment fee of 0.25 percent which is payable on the undisbursed
portion of the $50 million World Bank loan to the NPAF;
Interest of 7.25 percent payable on the disbursed portion of the $50 million
World Bank loan;
For purposes of the financial projections, annual operating costs are
conservatively estimated to be $1.145 million per year and are assumed to
increase at a rate of 3 percent per annum. Actual operating costs may be
somewhat lower, depending on the availability of lower cost local personnel
to conduct the technical appraisals and the success of the initial screening
review in minimizing the number of technical appraisals that do not result in
loan commitments.
2.     Annual operating costs consist of the following items:
*     Salaries, rent, and general operating expenses of $715,000;
*     Appraisal costs are $28,500 per appraisal. The NPAF appraises 15 projects per year,
of which 10 result in financeable projects and 5 result in rejected applications.
3.     Table A4.2 presents the 17 year operating results for the NPAF. The projections indicate that
the NPAF would incur cumulative operating losses of approximately $1.5 million during the first two
years and would generate its first operating profit in the third year. Table A4. 1 shows that the rate
of disbursement of funds for this base case is close to the IBRD standard profile for lines of credit.

STAFF APPRAlSAL REPORT
RUSSN FEDEATION
ENVIRONMENTAL MANAGEMENT PRoJBcr
ANNEx 4.2
NATIONAL POLLUTION ABATEMENT FACILITY
TYPICAL PROJECT CONCEPTS
1.           The following is a list of typical pollution resource recovery pollution abatement
projects, which are all considered to be commercially viable. A more detailed list is currently being
compiled by the consultants that are working on the setting up of the NPAF.
2.          (a) Copper Dust Recovery. This potential project involves the recovery of dust from
a Nickel Smelter in the Murmansk region (Kola Peninsular) containing high concentrations of copper
and other toxic heavy metals and processing the dust to produce a high grade copper product for
export using a closed circuit low pollution recovery process. Appropriate cost of the project $20
million. Possible loan amount from the NPAF is $5 million for import of foreign technology and
equipment.
3.          (b)  Hydrocarbon Vapor Recovery.  Another project involves the recovery of
hydrocarbon vapors from large crude oil tank farms, which are currently being emitted to atmosphere
causing severe health and safety problems because of the toxicity of the vapors and their high
flammability. Investments in the range US$2-4 million may be required depending on the size of the
tank farm, of which there are possibly ten or more large scale ones in the Russian Federation.
Possibly up 100,000 metric tons/year of light fraction hydrocarbons can be captured as these sites and
processed at nearby refineries.
4.          (c) Copper Recovery from Waste Tailings. In the Urals region, waste tailings from
the mining and processing of iron ore contains high concentrations of copper (of equivalent ore grade),
which are currently being deposited in large tailings ponds. Due to natural oxidation processes and
action of sulphur oxidizing bacteria, the copper leaches of out of the tailings and contaminates surface
and ground waters. Using modern copper ore flotation methods with biodegradable low toxicity
flotation chemicals in closed cycle water circuits these copper ores can be separated to produce a high
grade copper concentrate. Through a tolling arrangement with a Russian smelter the copper
concentrate can be converted to a high grade copper product for export.
5.          (d) Oil Recovery. In some oil producing regions of Tyumen Oblast it is estimated
that up to 60 percent of the surface land and water resources are contaminated by oil spills. The sites
have a very considerable resource recovery potential using modem technology for oil spill recovery
and decontamination. Several technologies will be evaluated on a pilot basis under the World Bank
Second Oil Rehabilitation Loan. Investment will be needed to procure the most preferred technology
for a full scale project in one of the oil producing areas and recovered oil would be exported to
provide the revenue stream for repayment of the NPAF loan.
6.           The EMP Hazardous Waste Component includes a number of enterprise specific waste
related environmental management studies that will be offered as opportunities for donor funding. In
addition to being demonstrations of how improved waste management practices can be applied in



Annex 4.2                                                                            185
polluting industrial sectors for emulation elsewhere in the Russian Federation, these studies will be
designed to assist the particular enterprises involved in qualifying for financing from the National
Pollution Abatement Facility. The specific enterprises have been selected based on their future
viability and their ability to enhance productivity, profitability and export potential through the
application of clean technologies and resource recovery techniques in implementing improved waste
management practices. The scope of the study work to be undertaken will focus on identification of
key investments for technological change and/or infrastructure additions, evaluation of the economic
and environmental enhancements these may offer, and their documentation in the form of creditable
business plans and financing proposals. The following provides a brief overview of one such
enterprise with good prospects of meeting the qualification criteria of the NPAF.
Tula Catdge Works - Tul. This enterprise has been a major defense industry that
is now a joint stock company, which has converted approximately 80 percent of its
production capacity from munitions to consumer and industrial products, such as
vacuum cleaners, table ware, valves, chains, bellows and photographic equipment.
It is a major generator of metal finishing wastes, notably those from electroplating,
as are a number of other similar enterprises in the area. Recognizing both the
environmental impact of these waste discharges and the potential to develop a service
capability for the regions industry, they have identified the possibility to develop a
commercial treatment facility for heavy metals recovery that would service a sizeable
regional market.

NPAF PROJECT FLOW
Typical NPAF "Initial Review Criteria"
Financial:    1.    Confirm the viability of the repayment entity.
2.    Assess the portfolio risk.
3.    The payback period from D/D to maturity is a maximum 7 years.
4.    The target Rate of Return is  1.0%.
5.    The minimum advance = $350k.
6.    The maximum advance = $7.0 million.
7.    The participation level can be up to 87%
8.    Identify the need for a foreign exchange loan.
9.    Assess the eligibility for ESP financing and potential interest of ESP
participating banks.
Legal:       1.    Confirm the status of the commercial entity
2.    The entity must be licensed to borrow.
3.    The loan must be enforceable.
Environment: 1.    The project weighting must be determined.
2.    No adverse environmental effects must negate the benefit.
3.    There must be compliance with prevailing regulations.
Technical:   1.    Confirm that the concept is feasible.
2.    Confirm that the benefits are achievable.
3.    Establish that timescales are reasonable.
4.    Confirm that procurement approach is acceptable.
5.    Confirm the viability of the payment entity.

STAF APPRMAISAL REPORT
RUSSAN FEDERATION
ENVIRONMENTAL MANAGEMENT PROJECr
ANr 4.5
NATIONAL POLLUTION ABATEMENT FACILITY
ENVIRONMENTAL GUIDELINES AND PROCEDURESaI
A.    INTRODUCTION
1.            Even though at first sight it may be considered unnecessary to provide environmental
guidelines for a so called "National Pollution Abatement Facility", there are in fact three critical
considerations in relation to this "Facility" which require special environ,mental consideration: (i)
pollution abatement projects (even those concerned with resource recovery) can cause adverse
secondary environmental impacts if carried out in an inappropriate manner; (ii) potential for
environmental liability for on-going or past operations at the proposed site; and (iii) an evaluation of
the net environmental benefits accruing from the proposed project against the selection criteria and/or
priorities established for the NPAF.
2.            The first step in the environmental review process is an environmental screening of
projects, followed by an environmental analysis if the screening review shows a positive indication
for some or all of the three factors described above. However, a positive indication for item (iii) is
a necessary condition to proceed with any further processing of the project.
B.   ENVIRONMENTAL SCREENING OF PROJECTS
3.            Environmental screening is the process of deciding at an early stage what
environmental analysis, if any, will be required for a project. Screening will be carried out by an
environmental expert engaged by the Facility; screening of an average manufacturing project should
take an expert no more than four hours to complete if the initial project documentation is reasonably
complete.
4.            An outline of the screening memorandum to be used by the NPAF is shown in Annex
4.4.1. The screening process categories projects according to whether or not they need an
environmental assessment (A, B, or C), whether or not they need an environmental audit (1 or 0), or
whether it meets the environmental criteria established for project selection (yes or no). If the last
factor is positive, the screening should provide a clear description of the environmental analysis
required, and also indicate where the expert believes it necessary to bring in any additional expertise.
Screening results will be documented in the Environmental Screening Memorandum. The NPAF will
bear the cost of the environmental screening process.
24/ These Environmental Guidelines and Procedures in their fmal form will become part of the Operations Instructions for the NPAF. They
are consistent with the approach outlined in the European Bank's document "Conducting Environmental Due Diligence on Financial Intermediary
Projects", December 1993.



196                                                        Environmental Management Project
C.    ENVIRONMENTAL ANALYSIS
5.            The analysis, where required, will take the form of an environmental selection criteria
analysis, an environmental assessment and/or an environmental audit. As with the screening process,
environmental analysis will be performed by the experts engaged by the NPAF, and as necessary by
any additional specialists.
6.            Only those projects meeting the environmental selection criteria will be further
processed by the NPAF. Since the objective of the Facility is to select projects which significantly
reduce the environmental impacts of existing operations and which recover valuable resources, a
matrix has been devised (see Annex 4.4.2) to assist in this evaluation using a qualitative approach.
As a first screening, the project will be scored against the four principle categories designated by a
(P) in the first column of this matrix. A project would need to achieve a minimum of one "B"
weighing within the (P) categories. Such projects would then be scored against the subsidiary
categories designated as (S) in the first column of the matrix. Projects would be ranked as follows:
projects scoring more than three "A"s out of a maximum of seven would be categorized "Highest
Priority"; and projects scoring zero "A"s would be categorized "Lowest Priority", while those with
scores in-between these two extremes would be designated "Medium Priority". Projects in the
"highest" and at the top of the "medium" priority range would meet the selection criteria for the
Facility. Those in the lower range of the "medium" priority would need further evaluation while those
in the "lowest" priority range would fail to meet the criteria for project selection. As work progresses
under the Policy and Regulatory Support Component of EMP, however, the selection criteria
methodology will be further refined to better reflect the Russian Federation's priorities in addressing
industrial pollution control by sector and by region.
7.            An environmental assessment (EA) is an environmental study conducted to identify,
predict, evaluate, and mitigate the environmental impacts which may arise from the proposed project.
The purpose of the EA is to recognize environmental consequences early in a project cycle, so that
they can be taken into account in project design.  EAs identify ways of improving projects
environmentally by minimizing, mitigating or compensating for adverse impacts. An environmental
assessment will also include a description of the appropriate steps, if any, for public consultation on
the project. The scope of an environmental assessment will vary widely depending on the nature and
location of a project, and it is difficult to give accurate guidance on how long they will take and
therefore the associated costs. For environmental assessment purposes, projects will be categorized
in respect to their level of assessment as Category A, B, or C (Category C projects are most unlikely
to seek financing from the Facility but are included here for completeness).
8.            Category A Projects. Projects will be designated as Category A Projects in the event
that they are deemed to have the potential to cause a significant environmental impact. Category A
projects will require a full EA, a sample outline of which is attached as Annex 4.4.3. Projects that
are likely to be designated as Category A are those that have the potential to cause environmental
impacts outside of the immediate area of the project, and/or those which are in one of the industries
listed in Annex 4.4.3 (Schedule A). The NPAF will require that the investee company carry out a
full EA for Category A projects. Additionally, the Facility will require that the investee company,
in the case of Category A projects, notifies the affected public and local government authorities to
identify their concerns associated with the project as a first step in conducting the EA. Investee
companies would also be required to meet national regulations in relation to consultation with the
public and local government authorities, and for Environmental Impact Review by the competent
Russian authority.



Annex 4.5                                                                           197
9.            Category B Projects. Category B Projects are similar to those in Category A.
However, in the case of Category B projects, impacts can be readily identified and remedial measures
prescribed without the need for a full EA. Category B Projects will require a partial environmental
analysis, which is more limited in scope than a full EA and may involve, for example, specifying how
a project will meet environmental guidelines developed by local or national authorities.
Recommendations are to be consistent with environmental regulations and legislation. Projects are
likely to be designated as Category B projects if they are in one of the sectors listed in Schedule B of
Annex 4.4.3. The Facility will require with respect to Category B Projects that the investee company
carry out all requirements for public disclosure and participation in accordance with local and national
law.
10.          Category C Projects. Category C Projects are those which are deemed to have no
apparent potential environmental impact, and will not normally require an EA to be carried out.
Projects are likely to be designated as Category C Projects if they are in one of the sectors listed in
Schedule C of Annex 4.4.3 and are therefore, unlikely to be brought to the NPAF.
11.          An environmental audit is conducted to evaluate potential environmental liabilities
with on-going operations. It is usually necessary where a project involves the acquisition of a fixed
asset; under legislation currently being formulated in the Russian Federation, the new owner of the
asset is responsible for environmental liabilities when incurred prior to the transaction. The audit
identifies potential environmental concerns such as contaminated land on the site, lack of compliance
with national standards, inadequate safety procedures, etc. An environmental audit of a general
manufacturing facility typically involves a site visit by a 2 person team for 4-5 days, including the
preparation of a report and should cost in the order of US$4,000, if carried out by local consultants.
If contamination is found, and further work is required, the time and costs involved will obviously
rise. A standard format for environmental audits is shown in Annex 4.4.4.
D.  DETERMINATION OF OTHER ENVIRONMENTAL INFORMATION
REQUIREMENTS
12.          There may be opportunities in projects not requiring an audit or assessment to
incorporate environmental measures which would enhance the project without reducing efficiency.
Information concerning such opportunities may be requested from the investee.
E.    COMMISSIONING ENVIRONMENTAL ASSESSMENTS AND AUDITS
13.          Any entity, in which the Facility is proposing to invest and which has been found
through the screening procedure to require an environmental assessment or audit, will be required by
the Facility to commission such an analysis by environmental consultants with the necessary
capabilities at the expense of the investee company.
14.          Projects shall not be required to be assessed or audited as provided for in these
guidelines where the Facility is satisfied that the investee company has already carried out such
assessment or auditing, using environmental consultants of international standing. The Facility or its
independent consultant will review any such environmental assessments or audits to determine if they
are satisfactory as per the environmental review guidelines below.



198                                                       Environmental Management Project
F.   REVIEW OF ENVIRONMENTAL ASSESSMENT OR AUDIT
15.          As part of the investment process, the Facility shall ensure that:
i)    environmental analysis carried out in respect of a contemplated investment is reviewed
by the Facility and that environmental issues, including the status of public
participation, are documented in the investment file (a suggested format for
documenting the review is contained in the Environmental Review Memorandum
attached in Annex 4.4.5); and
ii)    conditions of compliance with any recommendations or implementation schedules
contained in the environmental analysis are appropriately defined and negotiated with
the investee company and, where appropriate, are incorporated into investment
agreements.
16.          The NPAF shall determine that both of the above have been satisfactorily completed
before deciding to proceed with an investment. The Facility will take all steps to monitor and ensure
compliance as are reasonable, having regard to the status of the Fund as a minority investor and the
circumstarces ef the investee company. The Fund shall not be obliged to disinvest in any instance
of non-compliance which comes to its attention.
17.          The NPAF shall ensure that a summary report is made available to the World Bank
with respect to environmental ana!ysis completed for any project in which an investment is made.
G.  NEGOTIATION OF ENVIRONMENTAL COVENANTS WITH BORROWERS
18.          A description of any such covenants should similarly be provided in the loan proposal.
H.    SUPERVISION OF ENVIRONMENTAL REQUIREMENTS
19.          Where environmental covenants have been agreed between the Facility and the
borrower or investee company, the Fund will need to take steps to ensure that, along with legal and
financial covenants, the environmental covenants are met during the life of the loan.

ENMONMFNTAL MANAGEMENT PROIEC
ANNEX 4.53
ENVIRONMENTAL ASSESSMENT: STANDARD REPORT FORMAT
EA reports analyze relevant and significant environmental issues to the degree of depth
and detail appropriate to the potential adverse effects of the project. The EA will be prepared in
consultation with the project designers and sponsors, and the affected commnunity (in accordance with
national regulations and legislation). The EA report provides information to support the design and
review of a project; is not a decision-making document in itself.
2.           The EA report should include:
An Executive Summary. The Summary should be prepared and submitted with the EA and
provides a concise statement of significant findings and recommended action for the project.
A Text containing the following elements:
i)    Project description in a geographic, ecological, social and temporal context,
and methodology for the EA;
ii)    Policy, legal and administrative framework within which the project is
situated;
iii)   Baseline data describing the project area and relevant physical, biological and
socio-economic conditions;
iv)    Discussion of steps taken to consult affected groups and interested parties, and
issues arising from the discussions.
v)    Environmental impacts. The beneficial and adverse environrental impacts
(including biological, physical, socio-economic impacts) likely to result from
the project should be identified, predicted and assessed in relation to
appropriate guidelines and standards. Impacts associated with construction
and operation of a project should normally be addressed separately. Impacts
should be assessed in quantitative terms wherever possible. The sensitivity
of the analysis to the quality and quantity of available data, key gaps in data
and other uncertainties should be discussed.
vi)    Measures to avoid or mitigate adverse impact and/or to enhance the
environmental benefits should be proposed.
vii)   Alternative approaches and options to the design, technology, location, size
and operations should be compared in environmental impact terms and
quantified, to the extent possible; and an indication should be given of the



202                                                        Environmental Management Project
main reasons for the choice recommended by the consultant, taking into
account the environmental effects;
viii)   A mitigation plan should be presented which proposes feasible and cost-
effective measures to avoid or to reduce adverse environmental impacts to
acceptable levels on a sustainable basis. This mitigation action plan should
provide details of work programs and schedules, capital and recurrent cost
estimates, institutional and training requirements which are in phase with all
stages of the project's implementation;
ix)    An assessment of the enviromnental and other relevant institutions associated
with the project, discussing their roles and capabilities as they relate to the
proposed project, should be provided, along with recommendations for
improvements.
x)     A monitoring plan should be submitted which addresses the monitoring of the
environmental impacts during and after project implementation, and the
performance of the mitigation measures which are part of any mitigation plan.
The plan should specify the type of monitoring, responsibility for monitoring,
costs and other inputs (e.g., training), and reporting requirements.
A&Dendices
i)     Names of those responsible for preparing EA;
ii)    Written material references used in preparing EA;
iii)    Lists of meetings held;
iv)    Records of public meetings and consultations, including list of attendees, in preparing
EA; and
v)     Technical data that may relate to the assessment but is too detailed to go in the main
text.

Environmental Assessment Category
Categorv B Projects
Significant potential impact which can be readily identified and quantified and for which remedial
measures can be prescribed without much difficulty. These projects will normally require more
limited environmental analysis than those in Category A. Such projects will be periodically reassessed
to ensure their categorization remains appropriate. Examples of projects in this category are:
*     Agro-Industrial and Agricultural Development Projects (medium and small scale);
*     Electrical Transmission Projects;
*     General Manufacturing;
*     Manufacture of Construction Materials and Cement Plants (medium and small scale);

*     Urban Development (medium and small scale)
SCHEDULE C
Environmental Assessment Category
Categorv C Projects
Insignificant potential impact not requiring environmental assessment. Opportunities to enhance
environmental benefits should be sought in these projects. Examples in this category are:
*     Education (except school construction);
*     Family Planning;
*     General Service Sector Activities;
*     Health (except hospital construction);
*     Nutrition;
*     Institutional Development;
*     Technical Assistance

ENVBtONMNNTAL MANAGEMUIT PROJECT
ANNEX 4.5.4
ENVIRONMENTAL AUDIT: STANDARD REPORT FORMAT
EXECUTIVE SUMMARY
Summarize background, what was done in the audit, the findings, the conclusions and
recommendations, including actions for improvement and for further investigation.
1.    INTRODUCTION
1.1    Background. Give reasons for the audit, e.g., part of company environmental program, pre-
acquisition audit. Give date and location of site-visit and who carried out the audit. Give names and
titles of key facility personnel who participated in the audit. Refer to key components of audit, e.g.,
audit protocol, questionnaire, plant visit, review of documents, interviews with personnel. Describe
scope of audit: review of environment, health and safety, or environment only? Acknowledge
cooperation of plant personnel.
1.2   Facility Operations. Describe briefly the site, principal buildings, main processes or activities,
and main products. Does it operate 24 hours per day? Avoid repetition with next section. Attach
site layout map.
2.    THE SITE
2.1    Location. Describe location of site, including nearest towns or villages, adjacent housing,
industry, agricultural land, location of rivers and other major areas of surface water, etc. Mention
other factors relevant to environmental liability, e.g., nearby schools, land subject to flooding.
Include maps of area showing exact location of plant.
2.2    Description. History and Environmental Setting. Describe the history of the site, e.g., past
owners and past processes, operations, and materials used. Describe key changes, such as demolitions
or replacements of buildings, where there were underground tanks, where waste was disposed of on-
site. Describe briefly the geological and hydrogeological setting (from plant information or desk
study).
3.  REVIEW OF ENVIRONMENTAL MANAGEMENT
3.1    Environmental Management Structure. Give key points on organization for environmental
management, who is responsible, how does environment tie in with other management areas? What
management systems, procedures, policies, etc. are there for environmental management? How are
responsibilities set out and communicated?
3.2    Air Emissions. Describe key air emissions and their sources. Has the facility identified all
air emissions and characterized them in terms of composition and quantity? Describe any air emission
monitoring carried out by plant. What regulations, permits, authorizations apply to the air emissions -



206                                                        Environmental Management Project
does the plant comply? Describe any items of non-compliance (refer to copies of relevant documents
in appendices). Describe any incidents relating to air emissions, any complaints and actions taken.
Describe any other deficiencies with respect to company policy, regulations or good practices.
3.3    Liquid Effluents. Describe key liquid effluents, how they arise and how/where they are
discharged from the site. Describe any effluent treatment which is done on-site. Describe all drainage
systems, including sanitary sewers and storm water/rain water drains (which may or may not be
separate) what regulations, consents, licenses apply to effluents - does the plant comply? Describe
any areas of non-compliance. (Refer to supporting documents in appendices.) Describe any incidents
relating to effluents, any complaints and action taken. What effluent monitoring is done by the
plant/water authorities? What is the potential for effluents to be contaminated by routine activities,
incidents, etc. - what measures or equipment are in place to reduce risk?
3.4    Waste Management. Describe key wastes and their sources (solid waste, liquids, hazardous
wastes, etc.). Has the facility identified all wastes and characterized them in terms of composition
and quantity? Describe any analysis of waste which the plant carries out. What regulations, permits,
etc, apply to the wastes - does the plant comply? Describe any non-compliance. (Refer to supporting
documents in appendices.) Describe any incidents relating to waste storage and disposal. Pay
particular attention to past practices regarding waste treatment and disposal.
3.5    Storage and Processing of Chemicals. Oils, and Solvents. Describe tank farms, individual
bulk tanks (above or below ground), drum storage areas, flammables processing or storage, toxic
gases or liquids processing or storage, location of storage areas, etc. Focus on spill prevention and
control. Do tanks have adequate bunding; is there containment if drums leak, if there is spill during
loading/unloading  of road tankers where does it go, etc?   What regulations apply to
chemicals/oil/solvent storage - does the plant comply? Describe any incidents relating to storage.
Describe past practices which have, or may have, caused environmental problems. Has the plant
inspection revealed evidence of spillage, leaking tanks/drums, etc. - if so describe. Have bulk tanks
been integrity tested. What are the maintenance inspection routines?
3.6    Noise. Describe sources of high noise levels and where these produce high noise levels off-
site. Has the plant conducted an off-site noise survey? What regulations apply on noise levels - does
the plant comply? Describe any non-compliance and public complaints.
3.7    PCBs. Describe any PCB containing electrical or hydraulic equipment in use at the facility.
Is it adequately identified and labeled? Is containment provided for spills? What procedures have
been used for any past PCB removal and disposal? (Refer to supporting documents in appendices.)
Identify contractors used for PCB disposal. Describe any on-going programs for PCB replacement.
Has the plant measured for possible PCB contamination?
3.8    Asbestos. Describe any uses of asbestos containing materials in the manufacturing activities
or in the building materials, insulation, etc. What regulations apply? Does the facility have clear
procedures for work in asbestos materials, removal of asbestos, etc. Describe any removal and
disposal of asbestos carried out by the plant and identify contractors used. Has asbestos been disposed
of on site.?
3.9    Emergency Plans. Describe briefly the emergency plans for dealing with environmental
incidents. Do these plans include involvement of local emergency services, communication with the
public, etc? Do they cover all types of incidents which could occur at or affect the plant. Identify



Annex 4.5.4                                                                       207
any deficiencies.
3.10 Housekeeping. Based on the facility inspection, comment on the standard of housekeeping
from an environmental and safety point of view. Is the plant maintained and operated in a tidy
manner? Does good housekeeping help minimize the risk of environmental and safety problems or
does bad housekeeping increase the risk? Give specific examples noted during the audit.
3.11   Groundwater and Contaminated Land.  Describe the potential for and any known
contamination of groundwater at the site. Is there any groundwater monitoring? Identify any
abstraction of groundwater either on site or nearby. Describe any potential for and any known
contamination of the ground. Has the plant conducted any sampling and investigation of soil. Refer
to any past surveys or investigation results. Is there any program for remedial action on contaminated
land?
4.    SURVEY OF COMPLIANCE WITH ENVIRONMENTAL LAWS, REGULATIONS
AND COMPANY POLICIES
4.1    Air Emissions
4.2.   Liquid Effluent
4.3    Waste
4.4    Contaminated Land
4.5    Companv Policy
Sununarize the key environmental regulations and compliance.  (Most of the relevant
regulations and areas of non-compliance will have been referred to in Section 3.)
S.    CONCLUSIONS AND RECOMMENDATIONS
Briefly set out key conclusions and recommendations with respect to:
*     compliance with regulations, company policy, etc.
*     environmental problems (actual or potential) at the site; and
*     actions which need to be taken to implement improvements.
Avoid conclusions, such as "there are no environmental problems at the site," and stick to the
factual conclusions.
6.    RECOMMENDATIONS FOR FURTHER INVESTIGATION
Set out any areas which require further investigation (e.g., soil sampling and analysis,
groundwater sampling, air emission measurements, effluent analysis) to confirm whether or not there
is an environmental problem.
7.    APPENDICES



208                                                       Environmental Management Project
8   PHOTOLOG
Use photos only where needed to help explain a finding or to make a point, and not just
generally to illustrate the report and show the facility.
9.    SUPPORTING DOCUMENTATION
Provide copies of principal permits, effluent analyses which show excursions beyond the
permitted limits, waste manifests, etc.

STAFF APPRAISAL REPORT
RussAN FEDAMoN
ENVIRONMFNrAL MANAGENMUT ftoJccr
ANNEx 6.2
ACCOUNTING AND FINANCIAL REPORTING PROCEDURES
A.    ACCOUNTING
1.           The Project Accounts include expenditures financed directly by the World Bank and
expenditures financed by the government and project entities. The Center for Project Preparation and
Implementation (CPPI) would have an accounting and control system capable of reliably recording and
reporting all financial transactions. This system must consist of two ledgers; one for US$ receipts and
expenditures and another for local currency Government appropriations and expenditures and must be
operational when project expenditures begin, capturing all transactions related to the project on a
monthly basis.
2.           All disbursements from the IBRD loan must be recorded as receipts in the US$ ledger,
on the day that the disbursement is made. Any government budget appropriations must be recorded
as receipts for the month that they relate to, in the local currency ledger. The two monthly ledgers
would be prepared by CPPI no later than ten business days after the end of the month.
3.           The components would be consolidated in US$ equivalents and filed to be used for
reporting purposes at the end of the quarter. As statements of expenditure (SOEs) and a Special
Account (SA) will be used in this project, the CPPI would be requested to prepare and maintain, on
a monthly basis: (a) a schedule of SOE expenditures and amounts, and (b) a summary of the SA
account activity and reconciliation with the SA balance in the commercial bank account and the project
account.
B.    FINANCIAL REPORTING
4.           The World Bank requires the financial performance and status of a project to be
monitored regularly during implementation, either during the period of loan disbursement or
throughout the life of the loan. The CPPI would provide quarterly and annual Project Accounts, and
reporting on the cash receipts and expenditures related to each component and the overall financial
performance of the project. The Project Accounts would not only include expenditures directly
financed by the World Bank, but also the expenditures financed by the government and project
entities. These reports would reflect actual component activity versus planned expenditure for the
most recent fiscal quarter, fiscal year-to-date and project inception-to-date. The format and individual
classification of receipts and expenditures were discussed and agreed upon between the Russian
Government and the World Bank during negotiations (Attachments 1 and 2).
5.           The quarterly reports will be summarized in a Consolidated Statement of Project
Receipts and Expenditures prepared using the US$ combined amounts. The consolidated report would
be rolled up from each sub-component, prepared using the US$ combined amounts (the summation
of the US$ receipts and expenditures, and the local currency receipts and expenditures translated to
US$ equivalents.)

STAFF APPRAISAL REPORT
RUSSIAN FEDERATION
ENVIRONMENTAL MANAGEMENT PROJEcr
ANNEX 7.3
CENTER FOR PROJECT PREPARATION AND IMPLEMETATION
TERMS OF REFERENCE
1.    The Center for Project Preparation and Implementation (CPPI), as a separate legal entity,
established under The Ministry of Environment and Natural Resources (MEPNR) Order and following
regulations contained in that Order, will be responsible for acting as service agency and a resource
center to facilitate preparation and implementation of the Technical Assistance components of the
World Bank-financed Environmental Management Project (EMP) as well as projects financed under
the Global Environment Facility (GEF) and other sources of funding from the intemational
community. The EMP comprises several components as follows:
1. Technical Assistance
1.1   Policy and Regulatory Support;
1.2   Environmental Epidemiology;
1.3    Water Quality and Water Resource Management;
1.4    Hazardous Waste Management;
2. National Pollution Abatement Facility; and
3. The Center for Project Preparation and Implementation.
2     Responsibility for project preparation and implementation will lie with the subcomponent
implementing agencies, both in Moscow and in the regions; the CPPI's role will be to support
implementation entities in these tasks in the following areas;
(a)    Liaison;
(b)    Procurement;
(c)    Disbursement;
(d)    Reporting, Accounting and Auditing:
(e)   Information exchange; and
(f)    Policies conceming the above.
The CPPI will be assisted by a consulting firm, hereinafter called the Project Management
Advisory (PMA) firm, engaged following the World Bank Guidelines on the Use of Consultants under
a separate Terms of Reference.
3.    Liaison:      The CPPI will provide liaison with donors, ministries, other public entities and
the Subcomponent Implementing Team (SITs) (and other entities already set up, or to be created to
manage project components) on project activities. Such liaison will include facilitating the interaction
of concerned entities and the provision of information as described in paragraph 7. In this regard,
the CPPI will be the consolidated repository for project information and data which it will make
available to concerned entities in appropriate formats. Also the CCPI will assist the MEPNR and the
regions in organizing and coordinating seminars and workshops to disseminate project progress, results



Annex 7.3                                                                        219
and lessons learned, both for the Russian Government, NGO and public audiences, and for non-
Russian interested entities.
4.    Procurement:  The CPPI will have general responsibility (and delegation of responsibility)
for the administration of the procurement of equipment, goods and services required for the Technical
Assistance components of the project (paragraph 1). In undertaking procurement of equipment and
goods, the CPPI will follow the World Bank Guidelines for Procurement under IBRD Loans and IDA
Credits and, for selecting and employing professional services, will follow the Guidelines for the Use
of Consultants by World Bank Borrowers and by the World Bank as Executing Agency. The CPPI
will also be familiar with and will follow the procurement provisions of the PPF Agreement Letter
and the Loan Agreement. In undertaking procurement activities, the CPPI will be assisted by the
Project Management Advisory firtn as noted in paragraph 1. The specific responsibilities and
arrangements for procurement will be as follows;
(i)    Equipment and Goods: The CPPI will have the responsibility for procuring all the
equipment required for the Technical Assistance Components and for the start up
equipment for the National Pollution Abatement Facility. In general, the equipment
to be procured will follow the lists given in the Procurement Annex to the IBRD Staff
Appraisal Report (SAR). However, as project preparation and implementation
progresses there may be amendments to these lists. The CPPI should consolidate the
lists, prepare specifications and confirm with implementing agencies and project
managers, that the specifications meet the needs of the project component. Wherever
possible, equipment needs should be combined in packages with ICB being used for
all packages with estimated values of over US$300,000. Some equipment will be
required later in the project cycle and if the equipment specifications are agreed, then
the CPPI should use its best judgement to determine whether: (a) to include this as
part of early packages with delayed delivery timed to best meet the needs of the
project; (b) procure with the bulk of the equipment and either store or deliver early
to the appropriate agency (bearing in mind possible security risks); or (c) whether to
procure the equipment separately when needed. Packages with an estimated value of
under US$300,000 may be procured through International Shopping. Local shopping
may be used for supplies and minor items readily available locally and, where bulk
procurement would not be more economical. Local shopping may be delegated to the
SITs, which may set up small imprest accounts to be funded by the CPPI.
(ii)   The selection and employment of professional services: The CPPI will act as a
service agency and facilitator for the selection and employment of professional
services. Such services may be provided from foreign and Russian sources by: (a)
consulting firms and individuals and (b) Institutes. Services also include hiring of
Russian Subcomponent Project Managers (SCPMs), both in Moscow and in the
regions and the Russian technical and support staff needed for the Project. In general,
all contracts for professional services will be signed with the CPPI, but professional
and technical supervision will be the responsibility of the SITs. For most contracts
with firms, payments will be made by the CPPI based on SIT or SCPM authorized
estimates of cash flow, with reconciliation taking place on a "trailing month" basis.
Depending on the location and organizational structure, payments (or salaries) for
individuals may be made as for firms, or may be made by SITs or SCPMs on a
payroll basis with the CPPI advancing funds to meet the payrolls in a timely manner.
For this purpose, agencies will be required to set up accounting procedures acceptable
to the CPPI (and the IBRD) and in compliance with Government regulations. Terms



220                                                        Environmental Management Project
of Reference (TOR) and job descriptions for services will be prepared by the entity
which is implementing and/or managing the services to be performed. The CPPI will
provide advice and dissemination of experience on the preparation of TORs. Selection
of consulting firms will be through evaluation of proposals received from a shortlist
of firms (not less than three, no more than six). Selection of individuals will be
through the evaluation of at least three CVs. The CPPI will provide support to
Selection Committees (SC) by assisting in the preparation of long lists of firms from
which the SC will choose the short list. Selection committees will usually be
convened by the SIT, or appropriate SCPM. While the CPPI will be represented on
selection committees, the majority of SC members should be involved with project
implementation. The CPPI will handle the mailing of the invitation package to the
shortlisted firms and receiving and recording the proposals. Given its rapid build up
of experience, the CPPI should jointly with the SCPM, negotiate contracts with the
consulting firms. Individual contracts will be negotiated by their supervisors on the
basis of a standard scale of salaries and conditions. In general, the CPPI will have the
right of "no objections" for higher level staff. For both firms and individuals,
standard contracts will be used. For firms this will be the World Bank Standard
Contract; for individuals, the standard individual contract of the CPPI. While the
MEPNR as the Bank's Borrower is responsible for the overall success of the project,
responsibility for a consultant's performance will lie with the SIT delegated to
supervise and administer the consultant's tasks. Such delegation will be in writing -
copy to the consulting firm or individual.
(iv)   Training and Advice: Based on the Bank's guidelines, the CPPI will prepare a
procurement manual which should amplify the procedures given in the Guidelines and
explain in detail the responsibilities and procedures to be followed by the Project
SITs. The CPPI will also provide training in professional services selection and
contract administration. The CPPI will maintain a library of terms of reference, job
descriptions, and contract documentation and will build up a data base of information
on consulting firms. The CPPI will also assist in the administrative matters related
to training workshops to be mounted by the implementing agencies and with training
and secondments overseas.
(v)    World Bank's Prior Review: The Bank's review for procurement of equipment and
goods for all contracts over US$300,000 (ICB) is detailed in Appendix 1 to the
Procurement Guidelines i.e. the Bank would need to review and give its no objections
to the complete bid package prior to bids being invited (including the proposed
advertisement) and the proposed contract award with a detailed report covering bid
opening and evaluation. For professional services where firms or institutes are being
invited, the Bank would need to give its "no objections" to the short list of firms to
be invited to submit proposals and the invitation package. Prior to negotiation, the
Bank would wish to receive the recommendations of the evaluation committee the with
the winning proposal, and the proposed negotiated contract prior to signature.
5.    Disbursement: The CPPI will be responsible for the disbursement of funds, the preparation
of withdrawal applications and the collection, maintenance of all relevant documents. The
Disbursement Handbook which details disbursement procedures for IBRD Loans, provides the
information on procedures and should be considered a part of these Terms of Reference. Withdrawal
applications will be fully documented, except for expenditures against contracts less than US$50,000



Annex 7.3                                                                        221
equivalent which will be made on certified Statements of Expenditures detailing the individual
transactions. The documents to support these expenditures will be retained by the CPPI for at least
one year after the receipt by the Bank of the audit report for the year in which the last disbursement
was made. This documentation will be made available for review by the auditors (see sections below
on "Reporting, Accounting and Auditing") and the Bank upon request.
6.    Project Preparation Facility: A PPF has been approved to finance some of the activities
related to the start-up of project implementation including the PMA and CPPI equipment to facilitate
the start-up of the CPPI and other project preparation activities. The CPPI will be responsible for the
operation of the Special Account which has been opened to facilitate the disbursement of PPF funds
in accordance with IBRD requirements.
7.    Reporting, Accounting and Auditing: The CPPI will establish a management information
system which, at a minimum, will cover:
(a)    All equipment and goods procurement activities;
(b)    All consultants and personnel employed under the Project;
(c)    All financial activities including payments and disbursements;
(d)    Project preparation and progress using appropriate CPM and PERT systems;
(e)    An accounting system following generally accepted international standards in order
to provide information on the receipt and use of funds and in line with the terms of
the PPF and the Loan Agreements. The system would ensure timely and accurate
accounting of all transactions under the PPF and the Loan, and a clear presentation
of financial information. It should enable identification of the use of all funds by
components and categories of equipment and goods procured and consultants and
personnel employed and paid under the project. The accounting system should reflect
the movement and receipts and payments through the Special Account with balances
agreed with monthly financial statements form the holding commercial bank and with
periodic statements from the World Bank; and
(f)    An auditing system to meet the requirements of the Government of the Russian
Federation and the World Bank.
Detailed requirements for the above, including the determination of responsibilities for the
provision of data and reports on subprojects, will be developed during the 6 month start-up phase of
the CPPI.
8.    Information Exchange:  The CPPI will ensure the organization and management of
information reporting and database maintenance to meet the needs of the project and donors and
lenders participating in the project. Information management will include that developed by the
systems in paragraph 7 above and will also include written reports, both as specified under the Loan
Agreement, but also as required for the dissemination of information to entities of the Government
of the Russian Federation, donors and to the participants in the project -- particularly those in the
regions.
9.    Employment of Personnel: The CPPI will develop personnel employment policies to ensure



222                                                       Environmental Management Project
appropriate consistency by all the project participants. Over and above the employment activities as
indicated in paragraph 4 above, the CPPI will engage individual experts for the purpose of staffing
the CPPI in accordance with the CPPI organizational chart attached.
10.   Development of CPPI Policies and Procedures: The detailed functions of the CPPI and its
structure, policies and operations will evolve over time -- particularly during the start-up phase. These
Terms of Reference provide a starting point for the CPPI operations. However, it is expected that
they will be revised, amplified and amended from time to time to more adequately meet the needs of
the project.
