SrAFF APPRAISAL REPORT
RUSSIAN FEDERATION
EN4VRONMENTAL MANAGEMENT PaOinCr
ANNEX 9.1
PROCUREMENT PLAN
I. TECHNICAL ASSISIANCE COMPONENTS
A.    General
1.    Procurement Administration.  The procurement plan and schedule for the project are
summarized in Table A9. 1.1. The CPPI will be responsible for all equipment procurement and for
the administrative aspects of the employment of consultants in accordance with the Loan Agreement.
In meeting this responsibility, the CPPI will be assisted by a Project Management Advisory (PMA)
firm and one of the firm's first tasks will be assist in setting up procedures, and training staff in
detailed procurement planning and scheduling, preparation of documents, inviting bids and quotations,
setting up procedures for receipt, public opening and recording of bids, evaluation, awarding of
contracts, and complying with the Bank's review and "no objections" requirements. The PMA will
also assist in setting up the CPPI office and computer equipment.
2.    Procurement Planning.  Typical procurement schedules covering ICB equipment and
consultant selection are given in the Project Implementation Manual. These schedules are consistent
with those being used on other Bank projects in the Russian Federation. Specific equipment and
consultant procurement schedules are also given in the Project Implementation Manual. Over time,
the CPPI will refine these schedules based on actual experience.
B.    Equipment
3.    Equipment procurement will be timed to meet the needs of the particular component. Thus,
while it might seem attractive to procure all computers in one package, because of storage difficulties
and possible security risks, some computers will be procured later in the implementation phase. The
alternative of phased delivery by the supplier might not allow users to take advantage of technology
upgrading.
4.    Documents.  The Bank's standard bidding documents in english will be used for the
procurement of equipment. These are available in Russian and will be held on computer by the CPPI.
5.    Methods of Procurement. Packages of equipment above US$300,000 will be procured
through ICB. Russian manufacturers competing under ICB would receive a preference in bid
evaluation of 15 percent of the CIF price, or the prevailing customs duty applicable to non-exempt
importers, whichever is the less, providing the value added to the product exceeds 20 percent of the
ex-factory bid price. For equipment and goods below an estimated contract value of US$300,000,
procurement will be through International Shopping.  Local shopping may be used for items and
packages below US$10,000 including regular office and technical supplies.
6.    Annex 9.2 lists the equipment to be procured for the project (excluding NPAF sub-loans).
The CPPI will prepare all regular office equipment specifications. However, because of their
specialist nature, specifications for technical equipment (e.g. monitoring and epidemiological



236                                                       Environmental Management Project
equipment) wi]l be prepared by the technical consultants for the subcomponents. The timing of
specification preparation is given in the relevant equipment procurement schedules.
7.    The project will require three different levels of computer. First, "scientific" level computers
will be required for the Enviromnental Epidemiology and NPAF components. These will require high
level, open operating systems of the UNIX type, or equivalent. They will also be using software for
which annual license fees are required. Second, most Subcomponent Implementation Agencies also
require computers with fast operating systems (586, Pentium or equivalent), 8MB RAM and memory
well in excess of 200MB. These have been termed "higher level" computers. Third, offices will
require both stand alone and linked "workstations".
8.    Depending on the size of the packages, most computer procurement will be through ICB and
will require specifications which allow reputable suppliers to bid. However, there are specific
requirements for the project computers. All the workstation computers must be capable of running
the same applications, interchanging data in a compatible format and, in some cases, sharing the same
applications. Higher level computers must also be capable of running workstation applications plus
those for which they are designed. Thus, all operating systems must be compatible and must also be
able to run MS-DOS applications. The computers must also be able to run widely recognized word
processing, spreadsheet, project management and data base applications. It would also be an
advantage if these applications were identical or compatible with those used by the Bank. Thus, while
the computer's operating system will not be specified, its required characteristics will be based on the
above requirements.
9.    Given the "off the shelf" nature of the higher level and workstation computers, a two stage
bidding procedure will not be adopted. However, technical merit will be taken into account in the
evaluation of bids.  The technical merit parameters will include (inter alia): speed of processor
running applications designed for it and also running in an "emulation" mode for other applications;
the length of time the supplier has been in business; and the servicing arrangements in Russia.
10.   Component equipment lists are given in the Project Implementation Manual.
11.    The Bank's Prior Review Requirements. For equipment procured for the Technical Assistance
Component of EMP: for all contracts greater than US$100,000, the Bank's prior review will be as
specified in Appendix 1 to the Bank's Guidelines for Procurement.
C.     Consulting Firms Contracts
12.   A list of the major consulting firm assignments is given in Annex 9.3.
13.   Procedures and Administration. Consultants will be selected and employed in accordance
with the Bank's Guidelines on the Use of Consultants. The CPPI will be responsible for developing
and administering this policy and will produce detailed procedures which all Subcomponent
Implementing Team (SITs) will follow. However, the procedures will be designed such that the
subcomponent management Committee (SCMC), SIT and subcomponent project manager (SCPM) will
have the major input into the actual selection of consulting firms and the professional management of
their contracts. Thus the CPPI will be responsible for administrative aspects of the selection and
employment process and for the routine administration of consultant contracts, with the SCPM being:
(a) responsible for the professional management of the consulting firm's assignment; and (b) the
recipient of the consulting firm's output.



Annex 9.1                                                                          237
14.    Estimated Costs. For budget purposes, foreign consulting services have been estimated on
the basis of US$15,000/month (US$20,000/month for managers) inclusive of social costs, overhead,
fee and overseas allowance. An additional amount of US$13,000/month has been allowed for living
costs, foreign and local travel and contingencies. Russian consulting firm rates have been estimated
at US$2,000-2,500/month.
15.    Consultants' Terms of Reference. The status of preparation of terms of reference for the
major consulting assignments is given in the Project Implementation Manual. Prior to inviting
proposals and, with the exception of the policy subcomponent training consultants, the terms of
reference for each subcomponent technical assistance assignment will be reviewed by the General
Consultant Firm (expected to be appointed September 1994), in conjunction with the SCMCs, SITs
and the SCPMs, and cleared by the Bank. The terms of reference for assignments later in the project
cycle will be drafted nearer the time when they are required.
16.   Selection Procedures. Above an estimated value of US$100,000, proposals will be invited
from a short list of consulting firms. Proposal evaluation will be on technical merit. However, a
budget for the assigmnent will be included in the Letter of Invitation as outlined in the Bank's
Guidelines.
17.   Selection Committees. Selection Committees will be convened by the SCMC responsible for
the assignment in accordance with CPPI procedures. The SCMC will work closely with the CPPI in
conducting the affairs of the Selection Committee. The CPPI will act as a resource, will provide
administrative support for the Committee, and will be represented on the Committee. However, the
appropriate SCMC will have majority representation on a Selection Committee.
18.   Data on Consulting Firms. The CPPI will be responsible for building and maintaining data
on consulting firms. The Bank will make available to the CPPI data from the Dacon system. The data
will also be made available to SCMCs, SITs, SCPMs and to the management staff of the NPAF.
19.   Documents. The Banks standard documentation will be used for consultant selection and
employment. The documents are available in Russian and, as for equipment, will be held on the CPPI
computer data base. The budget for the CPPI includes for the translation into Russian of the Bank's
Handbook on the Use of Consultants.
20.   Contracts.  In general, contracts with consulting firms will be of four years duration.
However, a contract over two years duration will include a provision requiring a major review after
the first 21 months to assess the consulting firm's performance and to determine the need for and/or
scope of the future work.
21.    Bank's Prior Review Requirements. For all consulting firm contracts over US$100,000 the
Bank would wish to receive for its review and clear the following:
Prior to Invitation.
(i)    The short list of firms proposed to be invited for an assignment;
(ii)   The Invitation Package including;



238                                                        Environmental Management Project
(a)   the proposed Terms of Reference and details of the assigmnent budget;
(b)   the Letter of Invitation and Supplementary Information for Consultants with
full details of the proposed evaluation procedure; and
(c)    Any variations from the Bank's standard contract.
Prior to contract Negotiations:
(a)    a copy of the winning proposal with the right to request copies of all
proposals if required.
Prior to contract signature:
(a)    a copy of the proposed contract with the final terms of reference.
After contract signature:
(a)   two confirmed copies of the signed contract.
D.    Contracts With Individual Consultants
22.    General. The costs of project personnel specifically engaged to prepare and implement the
project will be financed under the project. The project personnel include the Director and staff of the
CPPI, the SCPMs and SIT staff, and individual experts advising the SCMCs.
23.   Policies. The CPPI will be responsible for developing personnel policies such that there is
reasonable consistency in terms, conditions and benefits for all project consultants. A consultant scale
consistent with scales under other Bank financed projects, is currently under consideration by the
MEPNR.
24.    Selection. Selection of consultants under individual contracts will be on the basis of three CVs
with the selection being made by the SCMC. For higher level positions, the "no objections" of the
CPPI will be required. The Bank's "no objections" are required for all individual consultant contracts.
25.    Contracts. A contract for the employment of the Director of the CPPI (in Russian and
English) has been agreed with the Bank and, with appropriate modifications, will be used as a basis
for all individual consultant contracts. Where individual Russian and foreign experts will be employed
on a sub contract basis with the main subcomponent technical assistance consultants, the latter's
contract will be designed to cover these subcontracts. Unlike contracts for the employment of
consulting firms, where the contracting party is the CPPI, most individual consultant contracts will
be with the SITs. Individual consultant contracts will be of one year's duration, but may be extended
by mutual agreement.
26.   Payroll. To facilitate Bank replenishments of the Special Account, the CPPI will set up a
payroll accounting system and require SITs to set up similar payroll accounting systems acceptable
to the CPPI and to the Bank. Rather than require documentation to support payment to each individual
consultant, the Bank will accept the documentation certified by the CPPI covering payroll accounts.
With the exception noted in para 24 the Bank will not require its prior review of specific individual
consultant contracts, but reserves the right to review such contracts on a random basis.



Annex 9.1                                                                        239
E.    Studies
27.   The project includes for studies to be undertaken under each component. While the general
scope of most of the studies are known, preparation of detailed terms of reference will be carried out
by the SCPMs, SITs and subcomponent consulting firms. Selection and employment of consultants
to carry out the studies will be in accordance with the CPPI's procedures and the Bank's guidelines.
F.    Training
28.   All four Project TA components include training activities. With the CPPI, the General
Consulting Firm will be the focal point for facilitating training activities to achieve economies of scale
and to avoid duplication of effort. Above US$100,000, proposals would be invited from at least three
training institutions and these would be evaluated as for consulting firm assignments with the Bank's
prior review requirements being met.
29.   The Project Implementation Manual includes equipment lists, costs, schedules and consultant
selection schedules.
II.    THE NATIONAL POLLUTION ABATEMENT FACILITY
30.   ProcurementAdministration. Detailed procurement procedures for NPAF sub-borrowers have
been agreed in accordance with the provisions of the Bank's Loan Agreement. The CPPI will be
responsible for procurement by NPAF sub-borrowers in close liaison with the Facility's core
consultants. The CPPI will also assist with the selection and appointment of consultants for the NPAF
and for its sub-borrowers. The Bank's standard procurement documents in Russian and English will
be used with appropriate modifications to reflect the NPAF as the financing agency and for sub-
borrowers.
31.   Methods of Procurement. ICB will followed for all procurement packages above a threshold
of US$2 million with Russian suppliers receiving a margin of preference as noted in paragraph 5
above. The ICB requirement will be independent of the NPAF's participation. Thus ICB will be
followed, even if the NPAF will finance only 30 percent of a package. Below the US$2 million ICB
threshold packages will be procured by International Shopping (see Annex 9.4 for a sample format
for International Shopping) on the basis of price quotations obtained from at least three suppliers from
at least three countries eligible under the Guidelines, in accordance with procedures acceptable to the
Bank. Below $10,000 per contract procurement will be by Local Shopping awarded on the basis of
a comparison of price quotations obtained from at least three suppliers from the Russian Federation
eligible under the Guidelines, in accordance with procedures acceptable to the Bank.
32.   Items to be Procured. The items and packages to be procured are likely to be industrial in
nature. To maximize the impact of the NPAF in supporting pollution reduction and technology
improvement, the Facility is likely to target its financing for equipment and goods, leaving civil works
to be financed from the borrower's own resources. Where civil works are part of the equipment
package, this will be financed by the NPAF.
33.   The project will also finance office equipment for the NPAF; the equipment will be procured
for the Facility by the CPPI. The equipment is listed in the Project Implementation Manual.
34.   The Bank's Prior Review Requirements.  For each subloan the Bank would review all



240                                                     Environmental Management Project
documentation for procurement of equipment and goods over US$300,000 as detailed in Appendix 1
to the Procurement Guidelines, i.e. the Bank would need to review and give its no objections to the
complete bid package prior to bids being invited (including the proposed advertisement) and the
proposed contract award with a detailed report covering bid opening and evaluation.
35.   Consulting Firm Contracts. The NPAF will require its borrowers to follow its procedures
for the selection and employment of consultants. These procedures will follow the Bank's Guidelines
on the Use of Consultants. The NPAF will also follow the Bank's Guidelines when employing
technical assistance for its own use. Working with the CPPI, the NPAF will build up its own data base
on technical expertise and will use the Dacon information as an input.
36.   The Bank's Prior Renew Requirements. For consulting firm assignments over US$100,000
the Bank's review requirements would be as for other project consulting firm assignments as detailed
in paragraph 21 above.
